Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which the one manner so is that you make III cauteries, or IIII, in aligning according to the length of the mice, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not hasten your hand to all the cautery, and let the patient often turn on his back; and another manner of cautery so is that you heat the cautery which has II nerves, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is located at the mice, or where the ribs of the patient come towards the left, and let the elevations that you lift the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body. 
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After he puts the two inflamed nerves so that the heart is pierced from the other side, then treat fire with the cautery, and thus he will have four. And if you see, if it cauterizes at all the cautery to three nerves. 
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has had putrefaction for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures previously said. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy 
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not good for dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes". 
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the shoulder, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the thigh, and two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breast; and let the cauteries be very close to the hope of the heart. 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery uncovered for a long time to avoid putrefaction, and do not leave the patient's cure after the cautery; and healing would hasten, and the two intentions would be together with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be a key as we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been previously stated. 
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet 
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in a person who is hydrocephalic and are full of clear urine, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning. 
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not insert it too deep, lest you tighten the yellow wax, and let the cautery be of this form: 
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After make two cauteries on each leg at the point of a knife; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries exposed for a long time without cleaning, so that it may fester; after that, cure the other cures as we have said. 
de la menoison	of the menstruation 
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any remedies; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with much greenness, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, or the circular cautery; and four cauteries around the navel, all subtle clavules, and two cauteries on the hips. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the patient suffering, burn him on the shoulder, and burn each one, and two small burns on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is profitable when there is good help. 
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids 
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are at the fundament, one or several, and are old and are of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit, then make cauteries: III on the spine of the back, that which is all behind below the scapula spot by spot in a triangular shape, and I cautery below the buttock II two; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees swell the face, then on the face make I large cautery on the stomach, as it has been previously said, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the cautery clavile; and leave the cautery open for a long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the place so that it is healed. 
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is named "thelul" 
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cope the alum, if you heat the cautery so that it resembles a razor, and then put it all ablaze on the said alum covered; and leave it so long as your hand and the cautery arrive at the origin of the vein, where the blood cuts; do this once or twice, and if there is much alum, cauterize each one as we have said; afterward the cure with ointments that are profitable until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the alum, it will be of greater aid. 
de plaie mal curee	from a poorly healed wound 
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or incision, which we will discuss in their place, then comes a disease that can only be healed by cautery. 
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula occurs, and it is old and has gangrene and putrid moisture, if you must test its depth at once with a subtle probe, and be careful that you know at once the depth of the probe. 
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After you heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tentacle has entered, and restart the cautery until the flesh, rotten and corrupted, is burned once, or twice, or thrice, according to the quantity needed; and beware of burning the nerves which are nearby, and the large veins. 
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, be careful of these places, and do not make this incision except in a fleshy place, and think that it is not dangerous; after curing the place until it is healed, and if the fistula is clean, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the fistula is completely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the fistula is bad, and corrupts the bone at its base; and as one of those that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	Of the illness of the kidneys 
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes as rains, and from strong windiness, and does not take any pleasure of a woman, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the rains on one side and the other with the pointed cautery that we have said before; and if we cauterize them in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will do more help. 
de la vessie	of the bladder 
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the back part above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic region begin, on the right and left, and let each cautery be as long as the nail of a thumb; and make one cautery on the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauteries be shaped according to the form previously mentioned. 
de la marris	Of the marrow 
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not allow conception to occur, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to make III cauteries around the vulva, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and II cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be sharp, as we have said. 
de la hainche	of the hip 
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous humors descend to the socket of the hip and for this reason it moves from its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the two bones of the joint are found, then you must cauterize the patient on the socket of the hip with a cautery resembling a circle, and mark in front of the place around the socket as it returns, so that the socket is within the circle; and let the cautery be such as those with which one has cauterized the stomach. 
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present for you, make three large olive-wood cauteries, and let the cauteries be as perfect as all the hearts; and cauterize until it is healed. 
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip 
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of that which we have said in the division, and the cure is not effective, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-looking pills. 
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After making the cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two ways: that is to say together burning medicines, and fire cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery can be done in many ways, one of which is this: you cauterize on the flesh of the hip three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and large, and have between each cautery a space the thickness of a thumb, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped. 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cautery should be applied to a dislocated hip with the circle we have previously described; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the whole hip and all the flesh of the thigh is burned. 
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done for sciatica when the pain stays in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh or leg. 
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, make two cauteries where the patient says the pain holds him, and four cauteries above the ankle, on the left side a point; and let the cauteries be knife-shaped, or burn the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as the toes or near there, cauterize him where he feels the pain three points, or four with the cautery which is called "points". 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, do more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, burn it with a knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient greater harm and contraction. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it until the leg was all swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the foot. 
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purging of the belly from which he had death. 
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery on one and the other, according to this manner. 
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise say about the cautery of the hip, this is how it is done. Make a tool like iron and let it be at the head as thick as a nail of a finger, or a bit less, and let there be spaces between them from one space to another with the amount of a knuckle; and let the spaces be opposite on two sides, and they should be like knots, and there is a handle made of iron well done. And this is the form: 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and feels hot, and then put it on the box of the bad hip, and turn it on the sound side; and the cauterizer once I cauterize and leave it for III days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the cure of anointing until it is healed. 
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery very little because of the fear of its appearance, and we rarely see anyone who uses it; and nevertheless, it is a good cautery for those who can endure it, and where it is applied. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The burning medical cauteries are made so that you make the instrument at intervals in which the edge descends from the gate and is of iron or steel with a long handle and with two notches and between each the quantity of the thickness of a fingernail; and they are open above and below and join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After you place the box of the hip on the patient lying down on their sound side; and press your hand firmly on the box of the hip; then put between the two circles of a heated awl that has been heated in the fire for one hour, letting the patient suffer the heat and burning. 
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it also finds a bite like that of fire; and when the bites have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the buttock with soft water, and leave it like this for III days, and put butter on it as much as what is black from the burn is removed; and leave III days for rot to draw out; and this would be the last help after the cure of ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or leg, make an instrument that holds firm according to what you have done in the hip similarly; and this is the manner of a hot awl, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot coals, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot. 
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Where there is a small opening, so that the point of a razor can enter; and put one pot upon another well sealed, and put alkali and hot water and sweet honey upon it, as much as there is two fingers deep above the powders until you have well prepared it in your hand; and leave it thus until clear water and slime or the sealed pot descends, then take all that liquid, and pour it upon hot water and alkali as before.  
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very sharp and is administered in the soft work of medicine and in cauteries of other members.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galien tells us of a remedy by which a man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic vein, and praised it greatly, and said that no other remedy was used, and that he was healed at once when this remedy was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches here after. 
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And say in this way that you take some fresh and dry green vitriol, and grind it well with a bit of grease, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for III hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning. 
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make it enter into a bath so much that its body is warmed through, and make it enter into bed, and the pain will go away entirely and it will be healed. 
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a fire cautery of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of humors. 
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat feces, it helps a lot; and it must be done in this way. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and put it on the fossa which is between the thumb and the finger which is called foscicle. 
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After you take some dry goat's hair, and ignite it until it is charred, then put it on the wool, and leave it until it goes out; and do this again, and do not stop doing this until you think by feeling that it has reached the hip, and the pain has ceased; and this way of cauterization is called "goat hair cautery". 
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain of the back 
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or by percussion or by excessive evacuation, or by similar matters of cold spread substance, none of these likenesses are worth cauteries except for that which comes from infusion of cold matter. 
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is fitting that after the patient has been purged of foul-smelling pills or other such things, you should make on their back, where the pain resides, three lines marked with ink, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be done according to the one called “point”; and if you see fit, make III cauteries or IIII with a medium-sized clavile cautery according to this form: 
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a tight ala when they rise, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes up on the other spines. 
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you are going to treat it, then cauterize it with a fire cautery according to this form. 
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery brands each part of the spine equally. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that when cauterizing around the spine with a pointed cautery, two or three lines are made and the points are close to one another.  
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and guard that you do not apply a cautery in gibbosity which is in spasm of nerve. 
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints 
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pains of joints are from moistures that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which the wise call "gout" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you burn on the face of the foot, then make a cautery with all the heat we call "a point". 
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come down to the knees and other joints, which happens often, then make a cautery on each knee three or four times on each side, with olive oil cauteries; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand strong except until the thickness of a grain of wheat is burned. 
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. 
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two points around the wrist; and if there remains no pain in the arms, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and take remedies. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give it good governance and purge phlegm, it will be healed with God's help. 
de la routure dou syfac	Of a fracture of the bone 
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes in anger, and the bowels descend to the hips and it is recent, it behooves that when you see it cured, that he does not eat anything that day; and that he uses things which loosen the belly so that the feces descends from his belly. After this make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath as long as the bowels are repaired, and reset them at your will, and sign with ink below the rupture on the bone where the knife points, and at all a sign which is like half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: 
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it gives off little drops. 
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bowels to their place; and have the assistant hold his hand so that they do not return backward; and work well on the patient's thighs, and put a cushion and a sergeant on the thighs, and another on the foot which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your strength, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone; and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you come to the bone; and be careful subtly that the eye does not protrude when you are doing the cautery; so that you do not burn it; and so that by this the patient does not die, or other harms. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your works are worth nothing. 
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of their bodies, and those for adults as large according to their measure; after III days treat the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; afterwards treat with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for XL days until the wound is well sealed; and it is necessary that his bandages be loosened often so that the boil does not protrude when he will go into chambers. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, give him a well-made bandage, and let him wear it for another 40 days; and let him have good rest, work little, and beware of too much drinking and eating, and of shouting too loudly; and when he follows these instructions, he will be completely healed. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the treatment of the waist in its chapter. 
de la routure dou ventre	Of the rupture of the belly 
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When fistulas come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then make the cautery hot according to its quantity, and burn a third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the place of the incision and make a line across the width above the break, and another behind, and hold your hand steady with the entire cautery. 
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and milder. 
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb 
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help it, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "points," and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its strength and its location, twists and its pain. 
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, start another cautery on top of the previous one. For this practice dictates that it should move to the limb closest to it, so you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed. 
de meselerie	from a mixture 
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The cautery is often helped by fire, and the same disease that comes from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy. 
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you want to cauterize it, be careful if the illness is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and it does not disappear or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the illness, then make him 5 cauterizations on the head: one in the nape of the neck, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the shoulder blade; and leave it long enough for the cauteries to reach the bone, and so that the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the thigh according to what is in front. 
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the malady is spread throughout; and it clearly wastes away, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have mentioned above, or one cautery on the head, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large one on the rump and another nearby, and two on each shoulder; and two on each elbow, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be wary of the nerves that are on the last bone of the foot, lest you burn them; and never make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you do with the cautery, the more help you give and increase the benefit; and know that the sick person does not feel any pain from the cautery as the healthy person feels it, because their body is already completely corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons. 
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After healing, apply flour of vicia with honey and other remedies until it is healed. 
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauteries on the limb according to its size; and let the cautery be a small puncture entering the thickness of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And one often does cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; and nevertheless no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the moving nerves in the body. 
de albaras	From white lead
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness which is called "albaras" is old, and the medicines are of no value, then cauterize a spot with fire, according to the quantity of the species of the heart, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and colocynth juice and almond juice, of each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it in the place until it is healed. 
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of a chancre by cautery 
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a sore first appears, and you see it begin to spread, cauterize it with a fire cautery that resembles a circle, encircling the whole sore. 
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nonetheless the surgeons say that one should apply a cautery also in the middle of the ulcer; and nonetheless this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen several times; and a better thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circular", as we have said in the description of cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot move 
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it takes time to die, either because of the excess that it causes or because of the weakness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old) and he has little blood, or because of time; and you want to hasten its death: then the cautery maker surrounds it with many small cauterizations by pricking; afterward he leaves it like that. 
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die. 
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through the entire cautery, heat the cautery according to its shape: 
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that illness which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it behind in such a way that the course of the rot is relieved. 
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment as long as it is perfectly healed. 
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron 
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of sickness there is which is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a consuming of the limb, for it eats the limbs just as fire eats dry reeds. 
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can endure fire cautery together, then heat the small and large cauterizing irons according to what suits the location of the illness; after cauterize all around until you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing remains, so that everything corrupted is removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the wounds cauterized soft bread with oil as long as the burns from fire are removed, and all the corruption. 
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds generating flesh. 
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then start the cautery again on that which remains corrupted. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this ailment has sometimes been cured with a hot iron instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for a hot iron in the division: take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the leeches that come to the feet 
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that from the fire a disease is born which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large thing lacking which harms the foot. 
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two manners. 
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and hot iron cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is if you heat the cautery sharp as a goose quill, and it should be made of good iron to the measure that it can encompass the nail on all sides, and that it has delicate edges; then put it all hot upon the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and leave it thus for III days until it begins to rot; then make a plaster of wild mallows crushed with salt, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall and be uprooted from its roots. 
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place of inflammation by applying ointment until it is healed. 
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and it often happens in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you administer a hot cautery; and it is in this manner: take a cane of iron or of wood, or a goose quill, and put it on the wart and the nail; that is to say, corns and warts; and put the cane on so that it covers all around, then he puts a piece of burning coal, and holds his hand well, and presses his hand while turning so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the wart, and can find the hot cautery path deep down to the root; and let the patient suffer the bite of the hot cautery for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will pull out all its roots.  
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Then do one after another, until you pull out all those that are on the body, then treat the inflammations which breed flesh. 
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling 
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from coldness of nerves, or from a quartane fever or another, it is fitting that you make them four cauteries or IV on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one on the foot, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery; let the trembling remain, and hasten the health from the cold sickness. 
des pustules puans	Of stinking pustules 
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes ulcers appear on the body, or stinking pustules, which come from corrupted substances. 
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	if it seems best when they appear that one should apply a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery from myrtle wood, with its point held in the fire, or from a long aristolochia root, or a lentil-shaped cautery. 
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further ahead, but the superfluity from which they come is broken up and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut 
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to a boil, or in the incision of an abscess, or by the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to staunch. 
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein and hold it very tight so that the blood is calmed beneath your finger and no drop issues forth; then apply several small and large olive cauteries to the fire until they are all red; then take one, large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is severed, and put the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger and hold the cautery there until the blood is restrained. 
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps while you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another cautery that is in the fire. 
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do one after the other until the blood is stopped; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well held back alone unless the artery is large; except by one of the four ways we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by a strong ligature of thread, or by medicines put on which have the power to hold blood; and let it be tied and strained tightly. 
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will apply rest by tightly binding with cloths or putting burning things on it, or other similar things, it will not profit, nor will it stop it. 
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has neither mirror nor medicine present, he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press well until it is rested upon the wound and upon the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it with cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood is frozen and thickened and rested; and make inquiries beforehand about those who need to cauterize and use medicines. 
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments 
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery, or burning medicine, and the ointments and causes and instruments and shapes of cauteries; and I have put this chapter from head to foot, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that one can find more easily what one wants. 
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this one, it behoves, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and therefore it requires greater caution. 
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein and incising an abscess and in the treatment of wounds and in the extraction of arrows and in cutting into stones and similar things where there is doubt and fear and many die. 
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. 
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for healing. 
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If people come who are so consumed by their illness that they die easily because of the severity of their disease and the intensity of its malice, then one must fear them. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are some who give you their sense and say, "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is spiteful. 
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not work rashly but wisely from those of whom you are certain, and of whom you can take oaths and pledges; and use prognostication and indication in the cures of your patients so that health may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good renown, and glory, and long memory. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen. 
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter in divisions by chapters, according to that which is before it, the chapter of cauteries, which I have divided from the beginning to the end so that you may more easily find that which you will need. 
dou chief plein d’aigue	sharp pain in the head 
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children at childbirth, and when the midwife pulls the child's head too hard; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown. 
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this disease except in children, and all those that I have seen hastened death; and for this reason it seems to me better to leave the work on such cures. 
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose shoulder was full of pain, and his head grew larger each day until he could no longer support it; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture gathered below the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and the workings are such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you split a wide fissure in the head; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture flows; and see here the shape of the spatula: 
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, like this: 
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs you see are that the commissures of the head are open on each side, and a sharp pain occurs when you press it inside with your hand, and it does not answer you: then it is necessary for you to split the top into three slashes according to this manner. 
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture. 
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After removing the bandages of cloths and powders, he puts wine and oil, and leaves it thus until the fifth day; then he unbinds it, and heals the wound with tents and ointments, and lets the main dressing be removed, and gives the patient dry meat free of moisture to eat so long as the limb is comforted and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the size of the abscess appears, and its assembly of sharpness; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left. 
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut there where the abscess opens, and empty it of its point, and make a suture according to your ability; and beware that you do not sever an artery; let blood flow until the patient dies from loss of blood and evacuation of moisture. 
de reume	from rheumatism 
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When a person has a sickness called “catarrh” in the eyes or breast and the sickness is old and treatment with medicine does not help, then the last resort is to cauterize using copper and cauterizing the two arteries. 
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you have seen them, let the patient bend his head back; after rubbing the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then draw out the patient's neck with the whole cloth; then look where the vein runs, and its veins are behind one ear and the other, and they are filled up; then mark the veins with chalk, then cut both with a sharp spathula of two parts, so that the blood vessel reaches the bone, and this is done by the breadth of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see it, put the spatula under the artery and the cup above, cutting as much as it should through. 
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if blood flows continuously upward. 
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space of three fingers, then cut from side to side and go down to the bone; and what it is necessary for the blood to put outside is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone without a bandage, so that the pus does not come, then strain the wound and tie it, and cure with ointment until it heals. 
de emigrainne	from emigration 
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes and acute catarrh, due to moisture from tears and the heats in the temples and the old sode forsenee and similar things, and it is treated by various medicinal cures and none of them help, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them as we have said. 
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of extracting them is such that the patient makes a rear of the hairs on his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is quite full except in some men who are too cold; and if it is full, let the patient tie his neck with some cloths, then rub the place with some coarse cloth, and raise the place with hot water so much that the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the shape: 
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then lift it up with tweezers and remove all the webs that are underneath from each side; and if the artery is thin, turn it at the point of a hook, then cut away from that part according to the quantity of the two heads. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not copied, it will not jump at all altogether. 
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain the blood from the sixth hour to the third; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that decay does not come before the suturing of the wound, and that blood flows; then cut away the excess which is between the two ligatures at that very hour, and afterwards, if you see fit, cauterize the wound with a hot iron to the bone until the flesh is cut; and this is a minor operation if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion. 
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is a help to end humors; for this reason it is of greater help against humors. 
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one should fill the place with old cotton and put well-made bandages on top; and when they are untied, let them be treated with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and bandages, until it is healed; and if there is a loss of blood from the artery as much as you work, hurry to cauterize it with fire, or apply vitriol to the place and hold it in your hand so that the blood stops; and if you do not have this available, put your finger on the place until the blood freezes, and apply cold water to the place until the blood stops and is removed as needed; and what is better and lighter for the extraction of arteries is that you cauterize the vein with a two-part trenchant cautery, but let the trenchants be well spaced to hold their heat longer. 
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat. 
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a space of one fist's width, and then when you have marked to cut the two sides, and you place the hot iron on top until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two; and they should be separated between the two sides because it is not soldered together at all; and this is the form of the cautery. 
des larmes	of tears 
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes descend into the veins that are above the temples of the head and no medicine helps, and you see the face of the patient reddening, and his forehead trembling as if from shivering; and where the veins are swollen and moist so that the hair on the paper is wetted, and the papers themselves are heated and scorched by the burning of the tears, then this cure is needed.
