Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the "cure contuse," and what you do for a patient who has this ailment is make him shave the hairs on his forehead; then make three incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as long as two thumbs all across the forehead going down just below the hairline, and the other two as two ribs placed above the temples, and be careful not to cut into the arteries that are by the sides above the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound be the length of three thumbs in depth; and have ready a piece of sponge and plenty of cloths for wiping up the blood, then apply the spatulum sharp on both ends which has this shape: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is behind the temple to the second incision; and flay all the flesh which is between the two cuts down to the soft tissue that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other one and then extract this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called “cultellaire” into the first opening, it is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other. 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the sharp side toward the burning flesh at the heart, and the blunt side toward the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle fissure. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the veins as far as the incision is continuous until it reaches those that open to the heart; and then make another incision in the middle, down to the other side; and then extract the blood equally, and press the area for the extracted blood; then put a tent of old cotton into each incision; and put soft cloths soaked in wine, oil, and ashes on top, and watch that no abscesses arise; and on the third day untie the ligatures, and apply a large compress of hot water, then cure with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other remedies used for treating wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	for the pain of the eyes 
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a sharp catarrh occurs habitually, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weaken sight, and papers burned; and hair falls out, and the head is filled with acute pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that those humors and this catarrh do not come except from many veins, and the mother cure which it has, if it is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you must instruct the patient to hold their forehead taut, then make a large cut between the eyebrows and another one down the bridge of the nose. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be until the bone; and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples that move at meals; and when the bone is uncovered, if you wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sever between the two lips of the fissure and put old cotton, and linen tents; then bind over softened cloths in wine and oil, and beware of a hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until the flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying things, which cause charring. 
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour flowers, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and administer it in these wounds to draw flesh all around. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of the ears 
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that lodges in the ears is one of four things: either grains, or an animal, or a stone from a mine or similar things such as iron; or seed, such as oats, beans, peas; or something flowing such as water and easily flowing things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When there is a stone in the ear or some other thing that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear, then put the ear in the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone and it discharges any drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then proceed with its extraction; and make him sneeze on purpose, and he plugs his nostrils when the sneezes come, and puts pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear above. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times fire comes forth through this treatment; and if it does not come forth, then administer extraction with fine pincers, of which the form is thus: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the pincers, it is good; if not, then do extraction with an awl of small size; and if it does not jump out this way, make a cane of elder and push the head of the cane or hole of the ear strongly, and plug that which is around the cane with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the cane; then draw it forth forcefully, for very often it comes forth as we have said; and if it does not come forth in this manner, then take glue as one takes birds, and put on some instrument suitable for this, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it may be, and draw it forth. 
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump out from all of these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear as an abscess hot vein comes, and spasm; and the manner of the incision is such that you make the patient healthy from the cephalic, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or place depends; and let the incision be as a crescent moon until you come to the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a fine spatula according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with subtle pincers and a suction device as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	When a sharp pain occurs in the ear, instruct the patient to first use a sneeze-inducing remedy, and then fill the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the pain is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps strong through this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, light and warm them slightly in the fire; then place one or two holes on the patient's ear, and strike from below with another stone on the other side, striking it with another stone that is held in the hand. Do not cease doing this with stone after stone until the sharp point has completely gone out, and thus it will all go out; and if you see, take a wire, and put one end into the ear, and light the other end with fire until the thinnest wire burns; then repeat the same process with other wires until the sharp point has completely gone out, as we have said for stones. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large body that one can feel it, then use forceps for its extraction; and this is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms that have burrowed into the ears, if you treat them as we have said in the section on treating distillations and the cure is not effective, then you should look at the ear in the sun: If any worms appear, remove them with delicate tweezers; and if none appear, take a cane of which this is the shape: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the finest point in the ear according to the amount of the patient's suffering, then suck out all the pus; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, then plug around the bone with cotton as I have said in stone; and if they do not come out strong as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the cutting out of worms, and you will find them where they treat distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, whose form is as you see: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is of silver or iron, three holes are made below the small perforations, and above it covers for distillation; and to press inside the distillation with an iron instrument well made for this, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point carefully with cotton; then he pours his oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the cane, and the cane is in the ear; then put the razor in all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or reached the ear; and let the patient smell it inside, and let the distillation be somewhat warmed by the fire thus it is distilled in the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of the ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a perforation in their ears; and the same thing happens to men by tearing of a wound, or by a splinter entering the ear, and this tearing sometimes comes perfectly into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there appears a small hole in the perforation, and one can see it well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes to you imperfectly, if it cannot be seen, is of affliction and healing in several positions; and where it can be seen it suits you to put the ear of the patient to the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent opilation, if the work has all this spatumile from which the form comes: 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind the entire plane, so that it does not bleach the ear; if the opilation is from flesh or cartilage of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and grasp lightly, until all the flesh is removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opilation is embedded perfectly in the ear, then take a delicate razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then apply it to the body of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the pulsation from which the patient complains of pain in the ear, pierce lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then put a tent into the ear according to the width of the puncture, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this no day while the wound is sewn, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on ground vitriol; and if you see swelling of the ear, it is necessary that you draw out the tent and insert another tent moistened in cerate which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, immerse a sponge and cloths in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding which are found in treatises on distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers 
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This remedy that comes in papers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary that you extend them with tongs and pincers, and the tip of a spatula from its roots; then put on the place ground glass. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without cutting off, the cautery with a lentil-shaped subtle cautery and then the cauterizer after the incision takes away what moves; and many times they heal, when nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return. 
de la gresle	from the gravel 
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come upon papers certain things that seem like hail in shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the operations are these: take care if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and this is an easy thing to know; then make two large incisions, then lightly scrape off the skin from each part, then take it with pincers and cut it out. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot close it without piercing a bit of paper, do not worry the patient; and if the tear is large, sew it with a suture and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not force it, for ointments will soon restore it and engender flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper over and extend the hailstone with pincers, and hold it with pressure on one side and the other; and if the paper is removed by an incision, it does not matter; and when the hailstone is cut off, pour warm salt water and cleanse the place where it was causing pain until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is smeared on cloths of paper above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it grieves their eyes greatly.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the excrement coming out. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is such that the patient puts his head in healthy air; and then take a linen drape and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity it contains exuding from each part, then put it on him; and press with your two hands on one side and the other so that the exudate is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp knife a slit no wider than the wound you make for opening a vein; and make the skin perfectly smooth as far as you come to the exudate; and in several positions comes exudate from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat. 
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Remove then in one piece of charred cloth between your fingers at the fire, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is dispersed; and take care that you do not insert into the fissure, so that you do not come to all the bone marrow up to the eye, lest you bleach it.  
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the arrowhead does not appear at the beginning of the incision, widen the incision slightly until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the area, and bind with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that has remained. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it until it is healed. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there comes a hot abscess to the place, then let the care of soothing plasters continue until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper 
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on warts other than those of nature and are aged, they harm them and cause various diseases such as habitual weeping and softening of the warts and albugine, as long as it is the cause of their destruction; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is before in this chapter on cautery, or by incision and suture, or by canes, according to what I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, insert a needle along all its thread above it; and let this be below the edge of the paper where the hairs grow near these hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs added, along the entire spatula cutting, from the large tear duct to the small; then remove the thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then sign on the paper a figure of an anchor, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raised by the paper which is divided into all. 
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is need for one to have a great quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make on all the spatumile on the two lines that you have signed and begin from the large tear to the small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the needle in one of the two angles of the heart, then flay it all; then bring together the two lips with a stitch of a needle with all the fine thread of wool, and wipe away the blood, and let the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows be without any sticky things, if you see fit to do this; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitch and the threads until three days or four; then treat the wound without a stitch with drying and constricting things, for the paper will be revived at the healing of the wound and its joining, but the stitch is useless (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear; and if there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have told, with three needles detached according to the form which is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take he who surpasses small strengths equally according to the form which is here: 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, take a needle with thread and put it in the shape; and put one thread near the large tear duct, and the second thread near the small one, and bring the threads together equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have said, then bring the two edges of the wound together by suturing, and care for it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs on the paper are converted: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in both is more skillful. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the canes is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and put it inside according to what I have said, and then make II canes by art, and II subtle ties as long as the paper and the width of the spatumile is; and cut at II parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on what protrudes from the oil paper, and strain the II canes of the II parties formed; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which grows strained will die and be healed and carry, as long as it seeks by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, so the cautery has one force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and if the paper is removed, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works are such that you take a fine needle and thread through it a fine silk thread; then gather the hairs and tie one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order in the chase another fine silk thread quickly, and tie the heads of the two threads; then put the patient's head on your knee; and let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for it is a subtle and small work, then push the needle all along the chase at the root of the hair chosen, and make it pierce the paper quickly as you draw it over the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the chase, and put it in the chase, if there are one or two or three or more; then pull out your hand so that the hairs come out all along the chase in the paper with the natural hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will treat the hair below at all the thread that you have ordered there, until the hair comes out through the hole above it, and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will treat the hair and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, as long as the hair grows in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hairs are small, you will accompany one long hair from a horse's tail, and let it grow with the one that you are leaving there, until it is elongated and then remove it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rotting of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacratio" or the rot comes to the eye, there are two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by a wound or a cut or a cautery and similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to work on it is that you split the suture and separate the edges of it and put flax tents inside and tie it until it is healed; and it is not right for you to use things in its treatment that dry up and restrict. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than the first; but it works with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose of aquile or althea and flaxseed are cooked, and ointments diachylon melted in any of the oils, and he wraps a tent, and cures him with this. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are such that you take care that it does not heal according to the shape it had before; and this work that we have said is nothing but directions for this disease, so that it does not return according to the shape it had before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye 
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is below, which is truly called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way to work in this case is that you take a needle with a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct as far as the right, so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh. Then spread the flesh above the entire needle and sew it up with a two-finger wide stitch. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is right, that is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the slit, and turn the paper, and make two slits on either side within the paper; and let the heads of the two slits be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make one angle so that when they are joined together, the figure is like the figure of a letter which has the name “I” Greek; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are affected below, from that which sustains the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then the cure of what we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a fissure or a seam or a cautery, it is fitting that you make a full fissure below the hairs of the skin, and according to what is said before; then separate between the two blades of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare everything in their power so that they may bring back the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is fitting for the work and instruments is in several dispositions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	of the wrapping of paper 
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs in many men in such a way that the paper above is stuck with the white of an egg and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it should be done so that you put the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and hold it with tweezers, as long as you cut what is exposed with a subtle scalpel, which is not too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient can only suffer from the scalpel being too sharp or the oil becomes cloudy; and let your incision, with which you remove the assembled area, be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and the entire assembled area is healed, and sometimes in salted lye water, and lifted with fresh water and coltsfoot; then place a linen tent between the paper and oil, and put woolen cloth soaked in plenty of egg white on top of the oil; and after the third day use lukewarm compresses and other soothing things as long as it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the corner of the eye 
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and resembles hard fat, and another which is not nervous, but resembles white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and one thinks to take hold as pincers, cannot be taken; and the one and the other resemblance begins towards the great tear duct, and grows little by little until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is such that the patient puts his head in good health, then he opens his eyes; and lifts the paper in your hand, then cuts the nail with small pincers, and stretches it above; then take a needle, and put a hair of horse, or cow, or ox, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and put it into the nail, and pierce it through the whole needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it above, and flay all along the side of the nail that follows the prunele and silk to the hair up to the head, then cut off the remaining part in the root of the tear to the whole spatumile subtly and with small forces, and leave the flesh natural or tearful so that by the incision the body does not shed accustomed tears; and sometimes the nail is stretched only on the fingernail alone, and on the thread, as we have said; then flay one along the whole spatumile according to what is its form: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the speculum does not touch the fleshy tissue and tear it, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision, drop into the eye a piece of silk thread, and with a collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the lancet cannot enter, often this resemblance of a nail is cured by medicines; and it grows as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, work the eye of the patient, and take a light spatula slightly sharpened according to this form: 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the splinter subtly, and if you see that it diminishes nothing and the razor approaches it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red lead and finely ground, and bandage the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as an abscess, then milk it and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh near the tear ducts harms the eye greatly, then suspend it with a thread and cover part of it, not all at once, so that fluid from tears does not come in; then distill into the red-hot eye a collyrium made of litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows upon the pupil 
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men, red flesh never grows, and it covers the eyelid and stays on the papers and is returned to the fire, and it looks like a rose of alabaster; and the works are such that the patient puts his head in healthy air, then he works the flesh, and all this flesh has suitable incisions for it, and he holds it with force; then cut the first piece of flesh, and go cutting with the razor until the end, and be careful not to bleed the eye at work; and let the incision be from the spatula that we have said in the incision of the fingernail, and with small forces of which one removes the scab, as the form after this chapter shows; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, apply oil of cypress or you put red wine vinegar and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the eye fire cotton with egg white, so that it is assured of a hot boil; and if there remains anything, and the pus rises above you, and you doubt a hot boil, leave the eye and treat the boil with soothing things for a hot boil; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as many pieces of flesh are added to the eye by this appearance. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless it is necessary that you relieve the cure of each weak part of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member endures that work. 
des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red that are covered above the eye, and they endure to the sight their work and weaken the eye all days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary therefore in the first place that you examine whether it is oil, where it is, and whether there is no other disease besides the oil; then treat the oil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, and suspend those veins at every corner according to his wisdom, and let the corners be subtle twofold according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be placed one after the other by degrees in the body according to this form: 
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then one should press those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after hour until you see those veins move away from the eye; and be careful that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very ardent in your work so that you do not cut through anything but those veins; and when you have done this, then instill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt what remains in the sebum. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all this in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of it, and leave it for some days until the pain is calmed and he is sure of the hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until he is healed; and this is the form of strength.  
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and hot medicinal water as I have said before, and it is not healed, then make a incision on the abscess where it should be located, and drain all the moisture from it until the bone is exposed. 
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, if it has all the instruments of which this is the form; and it is called "sharp chief", and is made of hard iron at the head end, and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form: 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two [hands], and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is healed; and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the fistula is soldered, and flesh grows, and the body of the gut is soldered and remains so for 40 days, and it does not renew nor become an abscess, and no bad accidents occur, know that it is healed; if this is not the case, if there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this method:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and remove your hand from the eye where you prick it.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the outflow of the eye 
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens completely and there is no clouding of vision or reduction in size, it is fitting that you bind the patient; then cleanse it, then apply cupping glasses or scarify without cutting to draw out blood, then put on the eye a linen made from acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye, and apply the plaster on top of bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough and double each one four times, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then strain it with a hard bandage formed above, and resume the cupping glasses to draw out blood without cutting; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the strained eye day and night, and if the linen becomes loose, it is fitting that you strain it very tightly; then remove the linen after day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, it is good; if not; resume the plaster and cloths and the linen and the cupping glasses until it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	For the rupture of a vein 
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes to the eye's veil, then it opens, and there come forth papers like grains of resin, and it is wonderful to see; then if you see it covered, the work is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the lower part, up to the upper part, then thrust another needle where the doubled thread is in the tear's part; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the place of the doubled thread and tie one part of the veil around it, and pull it well tight, then draw out the needle and put a soaked linen cloth on top well-soaked in egg white; and leave it until the threads grow together with the veil, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and at no time is the wound restrained by the veil on each side with a circle of cloth, until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great swelling, pierce it with a fine lancet that comes perfectly straight from the point, and drain the white moisture and reduce the swelling, and then extract the arrow as soon as possible. 
de la bowe de l’oil	from the gut of the eye 
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than bowel that is gathered in the eye, resembling descending fire, and it is not fire; and the manner of its appearance in surgery is such that you make the patient sit upon a prepared and upright seat, then take the head between your hands on two sides, and move it so that you see the bowel come up to your eyes; then be it ensnared, and do not let it descend and be relieved by light, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is fire, and if the descent of the bowel is not even as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a delicate spatula and place it on the cornea, making a cut along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea, until the bow rises; and when it has come out, pour into the eye sharp hot oil mixed with honey, or sharp water or fenugreek boiled with honey, and then let it be treated with another dressing until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	sharp things of the eye 
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen similar things in the incision, and those which are needed to pierce; so that one may work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, far from the light of the sun, and bind the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye to your left hand if the eye is left, or to your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the point of the instrument beside the crown at the thickness of a hair in the white of the eye towards the part where the smaller tear duct is located; then push the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously and turn your hand until it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that the almagda arrives at the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of the almagda be at the perfect measure of the space which is from the prune to the end of the black; and this is the crown of the eye; if you see the bone in this paper because of the clarity of the corneal tissue, then place the instrument up to where the point is, and then express it below one way after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it stings now, let the patient see in front of him and the instrument in his eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a short rest, and if the sharp pain returns through the second path, apply force with the instrument. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put a linen cloth or wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg yolk, and bind it with healthy oil. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on a common poultice with plenty of eggs. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have eyes too hard, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit," of which this is the form: 
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctive, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle spot, then apply almond paste, as we have said; and for the completion of the work, prepare the patient with the approaching doctor, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be devoid of all movements, and take light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same darkened house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then reapply the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not right for you to do this during the time of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary for you to delay this, because the humor rises hastily. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess comes, you must loosen the bandage before the seventh day and apply the remedy that soothes the abscess; and when it is appeased, remove the bandage and put on its face a piece of linen to cover for one more day; and let it stay in that dark room. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he must leave the house little by little, and return to his usual ways; and know that no disciples should interfere in this matter. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his land they made a sweet almond paste which sucked out the pus, but I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almond, so that those who do not know them may see them; and they are properly of almond: 
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the last one with three sharp angles. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh cut the birth 
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or arise various added warts, of which some appear like scorpions with many feet; and if there are such warts with a wart charmed of fire color, and also a wart in the form of good bone. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case of those humors which are sour and not putrefied, it is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands opposite the sun; and work on his nostrils, and pour vinegar onto those humors, and draw them out. Then take what you can hold with a fine spatula sharpened on one side, as long as you know that this humor is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything which you cannot take out, work on it with all the subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if it swells or an abscess appears, cut it as needed; and if these are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood is dried up and all the humors are removed, then pour honey mixed with wine. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the newborn's work, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is bone in the bone above, which the instruments cannot come through to cut: then it behoves you to put a thread of linen a bit thick, and knotted by hand, and have between each knot a space of a fingernail or less; and put the patient's head on the thread in his nostril at its best power, and pull while smelling so that it comes through the nostril into the mouth; and many times children do this at school, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the head which comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other head which comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them one after the other as we are who are on the thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as long as you know that the new flesh has corrupted that flesh, then draw out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the same place as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointments corrode everything that remains of the flesh; and then put on the nose a cane of lead for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, in which one distills the oils and medicines into the nose: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and you guide it similarly; and if you see [it], make a closed cane, and let the instrument be filled to purge the head; and have a handle at the top to hold it when you heat the oil or any liquor. 
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh out of the nose 
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" is born on the head and grows and becomes large until it is seen as something to be looked at; and for this reason it is necessary that you cut it off at the beginning, and remove all of the bone, then put on its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it while it grows large, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, because when one cuts it there comes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that it can be completely cut, then empty the patient and cut without fear, and treat the place with drying and restraining things. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
