Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then when this happens to anyone, if you look and see the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips together with a stitch, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core until they bleed, then bring the two lips together with a stitch, and remove it, and sprinkle powder upon powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put upon the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it comes out by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is such that you bring the solution together: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have let you know. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips 
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	When boils appear within the lips, resembling grains of millet, small and large; then you must turn back the lips and cut upon each one, taking them with forceps and cutting in each part; then apply the place after incision with pulverized vitriol until the blood is dried up; and then a poultice of flax, and treat the place with dry things until it is healed. 
de la char des gencives	from the flesh of the gums 
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a swollen lump arises on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary to hold it with forceps and cut it at its root and let the pus or blood flow out; then put powdered vitriol on the place, or other astringent and desiccant powders; and if the swelling returns after the incision, as it often does, cut it a second time and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of deafness 
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are accumulations at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scurf which is ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and citron-colored and green, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling; so it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands, and his head on your knee, and raise the teeth where the scurf appears, until there is nothing left; and do the same with blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other blemishes, until they are cleansed; and if one removes what was at the first reason, it is good; if not, begin again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because the razor with which one removes surface teeth has other forms than those with which one removes teeth between them; and these forms and others be prepared by you. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat a tooth for its pain that you delay the extraction as much as you can, for it ought not to be done; for it is a very noble substance until one has no excuse for extracting. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to pull, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth pulling. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is a toothache, and they have the good tooth pulled; but nevertheless, the pain does not depart because of this, as long as the evil remains, for we have often tried to do this with these healers; and when you are well sure of the aching tooth, then you must flay around the tooth at all its edges; then move it to your two hands or with subtle forceps at the first prick and prick, until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the forceps; and let the patient's jaw be in your lap between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert its point into each side lightly, and move it around as you did before. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and gnawed, then you should fill it with cloths, where the holes are; and if you extract it subtly with forceps, so that it does not break when extracted; and you must work very carefully around the gum to remove the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and a part remains, and return to the patient through the malice of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to do as ignorant healers do, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the bone, and don't achieve what we have said; but they often bring a greater illness through the roots that remain, or through the bone that they break, as we have often seen. And when the density is great, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if discharge of blood comes, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol; and if this doesn't work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments with which one must pull out the teeth first have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you are pulling out the tooth; and these are the forms: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large members so that they do not bend in the opposite direction, and they should be made of good iron, and they should have teeth to hold the pieces. 
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth 
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at the breast, it is fitting that you put on the place cotton moistened in butter for one or two days. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the flesh is softened, then he puts in the tongs which are called "algefri", with which the head seems like a beak of a bird; and they are made inside like a file and that's its shape. 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is fitting that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say, a pincers, of which this is the form: 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out because of this, it is good; if not, help yourself with all the instruments, from which the shapes come hereafter: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two handles, of which this is the form: 
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are in front of it in relation to the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like large tongs, whose form is as follows: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that many dense instruments are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise master subtle finds by himself his own instrument according to what his works and the illness show him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of others, lest it breaks the chariot or the other bones, where it rots, if he seeks the instruments that suit it, as I told you, and helps you with gestures. 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and strong to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can hold it and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if you have all these instruments. 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course of the body and the form is ugly, and especially in virgin women, it is fitting that you know if the tooth was born after the tooth and is not in its right place, and it cannot be treated or filed: then the file; and if it is attached with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a small beak, and is of steel sharpened at the top: 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the knife bit by bit in my hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file with a part of the file as it is shaped like this: 
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little in the hand gently, so that it does not move until it falls out; then smooth it at the end with no razor at all, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bites the tongue, then it is necessary to file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens 
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth loosens, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on what they are chewing without pain, and you have treated it with restrictive medicines, and this does not work; then you must restrict it with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that you can straighten the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the loose tooth or teeth between them, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again until the part where you started, and pull your hand subtly and gently, so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the head of the bone with pliers and assemble them.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, if you put it back in its place, again and again, as we have said; and no one interferes who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes make the shape of a cow bone tooth, and put it where the defect is, and extract it as we have said, and let it stay and serve for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the ligament of the tongue 
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this string which comes below the tongue by nature, one is born with it; or through an accident of a stitched wound; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your lap, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous string broadly, as long as the tongue is loosened from its hold, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from stitching of a wound, then he puts in the hook and cuts broadly that tie; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery which is below; and when you have done it, lift the place with sharp rose water and alum, or sharp cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and the patient nurses each night so that the wound cannot heal. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with a lentil-shaped cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it is of a dark color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, then cut it with an incision knife, and make it from a fine scalpel, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the pus comes out to your work, put powdered vitriol on it until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift the place from all around, and cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat 
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come inside the throat lumps which are called "godath," and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dusky color, do not touch it with iron at all. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron at all, so as not to cause bleeding; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will cut it off, or it will break by itself; and if it is of a white color and the root is slender, prepare the instrument for cutting, but first look to see if the abscess is hot and has subsided. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head be in your hand, and open the mouth and take the instrument between your hands, and press the tongue below all the instruments, so it is shaped; and it is made of silver or fine steel as a knife. 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue against all these instruments and see the abscess, take the lancet and put it in the almond, and hold it tight on top as much as possible; and don't pull anything from the cloths with it, then attach it to the instrument, which has a shape that seems like one force; and although the heads are bent and one against the other, they are very sharp and made of hardened iron or silver. 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then take pincers, of which this is the shape: 
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner; then gargle the patient with hot water, which is hot and easy; and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water in which cooked pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves are boiled, or similar things, until the blood stops; then cure it until it is healed; and if at any time other abscesses arise in the throat than the two almonds, cut them similarly as the two almonds. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, that is to say, an abscess of small sense; and it had almost completely closed the whole throat so that the woman could not breathe through the passage which was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she remained so for one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high up that he had to put two reins through the two holes of the nose. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then quickly, and put an instrument into one nostril, then the traitor was pierced through, and a large portion of bowels were taken.
de l’uve	of the eye 
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the humor descends to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below thick and round, it is called "eye". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the healing does not profit, and you see that the boil is soothed, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and the one that is round assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or of a yellow color or black, then you must avoid cutting into it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger upon the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue against the instrument of which we have made mention before; then insert the oncin into the eye, and draw it down below, and cut with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you not cut away more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut away more, it grieves the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two tonsils, and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of being cut, it is fitting that you use something to deaden the sensation of fear during cautery. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and burning. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And let the patient put his head in clean water, and then press his tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned or the chapter of cautery, and confiscate it with a sharp, fine point, so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and use the end of this instrument.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have on his head a hair or where one puts the medicine, as the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine above the eye; and let the patient lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine within, so that it does not descend into the throat, nor the bleating; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it upon the eye, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it shrink and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton in its sheath above, until the cotton ignites above the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and let it rest for four days or five. And if you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, so restart it, and after the cautery wipe it around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and purify what is around the medicine; and let it be washed with cold water, and cured with gargles until it is healed. 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calament and wormwood and oregano and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and add water and boil it; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot, place the instrument as follows: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it is of silver or iron, and let one of the heads be put into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, as long as the eye is mortified; then begin again often, until the eye dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the arrival of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not do this except at the decline of a hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put inside the head a chickpea of egg so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for a chickpea of egg does not make the vapor burden the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with safety. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fishbone, or something else gets stuck in the throat. So it is necessary that you draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all your instruments so that you can see the thing move; and what you cannot see and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if it loosens the thing through vomiting. Or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will come loose, and then you will draw it out forcefully; and if it does not come out from what we have said, then take an instrument of plumb according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they may more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest all life depart from it, nor push any bone inside; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows where the thing is airy; if it goes down, or he pulls it out forcefully with the whole instrument equally, as long as it is pulled out. 
de la sansue de la gorge	of the bloodletting of the throat 
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes medicine is enough, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not profit at all, then look into the throat of the sick person in the sun, then press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, treat it with all its small hooks or with subtle tongs that are fit for it. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a cane with a reed, and put it in the throat of the patient, then put the end of the cane with a hot iron, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient hold an ache all day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and work the mouth open, and the throat in like swallowing, and move it often with your hand; and as soon as the tooth feels the cold, it will die. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall back into place as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will come back without difficulty. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is such that you take a pot where it has live coals and let it be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that hole put the head of the instrument; then you begin your fumigation, and the patient puts the top of the cane in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape but comes up to the nostrils; and the nostrils will now run, and if they do not, you begin the fumigation many times; and let the patient be thirsty, and have salty things and such, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for them to urinate freely by this method.  
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the sinus, is such that when one can see it, it resembles tongs bent to enter into the throat; and it has a resemblance to the beak of a sewing needle, and it has the roughness of a file, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and see here the shape: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses 
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many abscesses are similar, according to what memory will bring after this in this book, and they vary in perforations and size; and there are two manners by which one is its appearance itself, and the moisture it holds. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the wounds which are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses on the head are different from those on the fundament, and abscesses on fleshy parts are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work. 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one should not pierce, until the pus is ripe according to its maturity; and if to such as it befits to pierce when they are mature, and do not die according to their maturity, just like abscesses that are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints and it is left until it is rotten around, it may happen that the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; where it is near the fundament, pierce it even if it is dead; and it is not fitting that you pierce an unripe abscess without complete digestion, except for the one near the fundament, lest it rot entirely, become elongated within, and a fistula arises; and it cannot heal in due time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its fulfillment, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation in a higher place or more dependent place of the abscess, and where it appears movable; and let the perforation be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and near nerves and arteries, and in all its equal parts where there is no weeping. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, bend it according to the limb. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in fleshy tissue, it is worth noting that you should leave the perforation until it is confirmed to be in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it in front of these, the body will be lengthened by the poison from it, and is full of much filth; and perhaps harden the lips and its depths. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the limbs may need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is fitting that you make small openings in small abscesses, and large openings in large abscesses, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the heart, and cover it up; when it has become as soft as linens, and is dead, then it is fitting to do as one does for buboes: and if there are those that are split into three angles, and there are those that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the angers; and if there are those where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected great pus, and you pierce it, if you do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain some of it; then stopper the abscess until the next day, then drain something again without delay; do this many times from time to time, until all the pus comes out; even if the patient is weak, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit often leaps with the release of the bowels, and the patient may die by chance, and you are not to blame. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if you wipe the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a full slice, then apply strips of linen or fine cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many holes, then it is fitting that you put in each one a strip so that they come against one another; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have sewn it around, then it is fitting that you fill it with old cotton or a linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then loosen it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bloodletting occurs during your work, apply cold and fresh water, moisten the cloth, and put it on the bleeding area many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the discharge of blood persists, then administer treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book; and if it is winter time, and the boil or abscess is very nervous, then you should put on cloths and bandages softened in wine and hot oil; and if it is summer, and the boil is fleshy, then you must put on cloths softened in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and treat it as it should be, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter. 
des soros	of serums 
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small boils come on the head, they are often shaped like those on linen cloths, just like the spot of a pomegranate seed, and many are similar in appearance. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and others where there is moisture as well as pus; and if there are some that are hard and stony at the waist, there is no doubt whether the artery will oppose it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the hip is such that you must practice with every instrument which is called an "entromissoire," of which the form comes afterwards, what it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, make it pass through for a long time. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is removed, if you scrape without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, because it will return when you leave nothing; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply it to the wound and leave it until the next day; and this will carry away what has remained at night. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the dressing again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are sure that it does not move at night; then heal the wound with ointment suitable to it, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds firm and is greasy, then cauterize according to this form for a long time; and you cut off your ointments, and scarify it on all sides, and put all your treatment of drawing fire where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I have told you afterwards. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also make an abscess if it is pierced, from the waist and from the cure as I told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cautery on a festering abscess is lighter, because it is made of little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses are without moisture, and of these were the abscess that I cut or lanced from the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had made a cut in it, one would have done as much harm as cutting into a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or starting, for those which come at the head of children and at the roots of ears, the opening should always be in the lowest place possible, so that pus can flow out; and treat them as is appropriate. 
des scrophules	of scrofula 
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess occurs in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes it comes in other parts of the body, and they are many, and they are joined together. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its rib, just as the knot and the abscess on the head, as we have said; and there are many appearances of these scrofula. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some that are so malicious they will not obey health. 
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	When you see a wound with good disposition to heal and resembles the color of the body, and moves from every part and is not inflamed at the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the vein, and is not deep; then it is fitting that you scrape it over, and flay it from every part, and spread the two lips of the wound with ointments, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not scrape the nerve nor the vein, and let the scalpel be neither sharp nor cutting so that the hand does not slip, and do not move too far forward lest you scrape what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you scrape the vein or artery, and that does not let you work, then put in the wound ground vitriol, or some powders that staunch blood, and draw out the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work, until you complete it; then look at your fingertip to see if any small scrophulous ulcers remain, and excise them and cleanse them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not right that you cut out that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself without harm; then apply to the wound old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out all the scrofula, it is fitting that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you know how to cut the root of it, and draw strong, and sew as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce them where it appears dead; and pierce it as the one before said, in dependence, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, if the cure with ointment causes charring flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	from squinting 
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squint, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be scraped; and this should not be done by anyone, because all the veins and the lungs of the patient are at risk for those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the two almonds. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to lift the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation. 
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cleave the epiglottis, let us cleave it below three or four circles with a small incision across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the incision from the syfac, not in the cartilage; and those are suitable for the sectioning of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to the whole inch, then cleave the heart until it reaches the trachea; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the pharynx, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the trachea which flows out through the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew it all up without touching the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely open and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect is in the windpipe. 
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then place a splint on the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are protected from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in III days or in IIII. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and clean it, as long as it was clean; and I will tell you what I have seen. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young woman take a knife and put it in her throat, and cut off part of the channels of her windpipe; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and although it had not struck a vein nor any conduit except the throat, the veins were strong through the wound. 
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound and treated it until it was healed; and nothing further happened to the maiden except that her voice became hoarse, and she returned afterward to her normal state; therefore I say that one should not fear in cutting the epiglottis. 
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat 
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of yellow, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no cause. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fat to us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess which comes from our arteries; and there is fear, and it does not suit to work with great fire except in that which is small, and probe and search at all the entryways: if you find it as I said fat, and cannot go into any vein, then cut it off, as one cuts off tumors, and treat it with all its covering, if there is any point; and bind it well soon, and cure it as it suits, until it is perfectly healed.  
des nous	of us 
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways there are to us, of which I will tell all the resemblances; and now it behooves me to say all the difference that is between us and issue. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that inflammation is heat and fever lasting as long as the boiling is not passed and putrefaction is accomplished, then fever and heat subside. 
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With new growth there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a pea, and grows large; and they are according to two appearances, either fat or moist, and many of them are of the color as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a wound, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument which is called “entromissoire”, according to its shape or chapter which follows. 
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of incising abscesses of us is that you take or the moistest place that you find in the abscess and turn your two fingers little by little until you know that the instrument has pierced the core then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the introducer, and take care lest it leap out. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs clear, whatever color it may be, cut the skin as I have said for other abscesses; and if after cutting with the incision no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty; then cut in a cross, take hold of it with forceps, and lightly scrape it from each side and keep the cloth where it lies so that you draw it clean with the knife; and if you cannot draw it clean, draw it piece by piece until nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains there for a while, the nerve will return many times; and if there is even a small piece remaining that does not grieve you, apply some sharp corrosive powders to the wound, and extract the wound, and put soothing things on the hot abscess, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the nerve is large, cut the two edges of the wound, and cure it as those who are skilled in flesh.  
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or something similar happens and you hasten it, apply the place of ground vitriol, and leave it there for two or three days, until the wound dries up, and cools down the boiling of the blood; then return to cover what remains in the nut. 
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Look here at the forms of the instruments which are inserted, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three of these: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistulas; and they are also like the needles with which one sews charms, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those made of brass are worth more, and are better proven with black wax to encircle the curves of fistulas; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of pincers are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are pincers which have two bends in three ways also; and there are pincers which have three bends, and are also of three ways; and there are pincers which have two bends, and pincers of a single bend only, and are of three ways; and all this is necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these which one makes are cutting, and of such there are which do not cut more strongly than from one side, from which one flayed the veins, for this one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; and of these introducers are the small needles responded in handles, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three manners: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them more strongly than in fleshy places, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and angles, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling a flayer's tool, according to this form, from which one cauterizes blood:  
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at no time in the place where the veins and arteries are healthy, and at no time they return according to this great form: 
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, so much so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to proceed according to the form of these lines b to g. 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and fill the wound with medicine mixed with charcoal, then bring together the two edges of the wound in stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast droops down and is soft because of its size as happens to women, then cut it into two ribs above it, by two similar incisions; so that one holds the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in treatment until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or if the incision is not entirely made because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with softened cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining fat and flesh, then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits 
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are hard kinds of scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture. 
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those who contain moisture it is necessary that they be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.: 
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day. Then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment suitable for this until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a nature resembling scrofula, then cut it as we have said in the cutting of scrofula, and if the wound draws inward, then apply a cautery as we have said before. 
de la routure de l’artere	Of the breaking of the artery 
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is severed, and the skin above it is sewn together, then often abscesses come; and likewise it happens with a swollen vein and an abscess; and if the expert knows when it is due to the artery, the abscess will be long and straight; and when you feel it with your fingers, you will sense a pulling sensation; and when it is due to the vein, it will be round and appear red; and it is folly to cut open this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, at the elbows, or at the neck, and in many other places, and is very large.
