Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to remove the iron instrument and he who is at the head must also be removed, and in that which is swollen from an artery passing over the skin for a long time; then operate on the length as incisions, and beautifully detach the artery from its tissues, until it is uncovered; then put an awl under it and make it pierce through to the other side, and remove the artery with a double thread in two lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then prick the place that is between the two ties with a probe until the pus that is there comes out, and let the abscess be loosened; then apply the cure that draws out pus, until the ties shrink; then cure it with anointment following this one, until it is healed; and if the abscess is on the size of the vein, then you must hold in your hand what you can grasp from the abscess over all the skin, then put the awl under the place that you hold in your hand and make it pierce through, and have it a double thread so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I told you, or with a tie on one of the two sides with two strands of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads might come loose, put another awl over all the thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first awl, and remove the threads in four lengths; then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess of pus from the heart and leave what is tied; then put a softened cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply cures of bandages and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves 
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in arteries and veins, they also come in nerves when they are strained, or from excessive labor, and similar things. 
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and arms and in all their joints, and it is a painful abscess, its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many positions without pain; and when it is removed, the patient feels pain, and it is not perfectly formed like the body, but below the heart; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and the one that is in the joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would contract; and the one that is on the head or forehead, make the skin with a spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, take it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with an oncine, flay it, then bone and sew up the wound, and treat it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	Large hanging boils 
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and not elsewhere, a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms; it has delicate roots and thick heads; and there are small ones and large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, and had small roots, and were easily split open, and constantly oozed moisture. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied them and found one weighing eighteen ounces and the other six and a half. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist there often comes excessive bleeding, and if it doesn't stop, then quickly cauterize it; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision with the iron, take a thread of hemp well made, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the hemp thread until it seizes the artery, and bleeds through it without pain; and if the roots are large, fear to seize it directly due to the belly, but you can well seize half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to seize the tendon which is of a black color and poor texture and milky appearance. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of sores later. 
quant li boude ist fuer	When the arm is strong 
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from cautery of wound or fissure of the intestine, and is on the belly and in it are some of the bowels, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that cuts from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or from windiness; and if it is by rupture of the intestine and by the issue of the bowel, then the color of the abscess appears like the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and it opens from diverse issues. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the intestine coming out, then it is more diverse, and when you press on it at its sides it springs back up, and then returns, and perhaps if it is tightened, it swells greatly at the entrance of the bath and through hard work. 
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, it is recognized by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed according to a certain quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary that you leave the treatment. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you about the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the boueil, it is fitting that you command the patient to hold his breath, and be stretched out all straight, then sign around the whole swelling; then command him to grasp often between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed with all the spatula, then extend the half of the abscess above on all the great uncine; then bind it around with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the knot be loosened; then work the half of the abscess extended on the ligature, and put your index finger in, and take the intestine; if you find it caught by the ligature, loosen it, and push the intestine out of the belly cavity; and if you find the boueil, seize it with the uncine, and cut off the excess; and if the artery opposes you or the vein, go around well then return to your work and take II needles, and put II strong threads in, and put the II needles around what you have done in a cross shape that you make pierce through; then stretch the abscess into four places on the needles, and if you see fit, remove the needles and leave the place as long as it ripens, and let the dead flesh come off by itself; or cut it off when it becomes thin and rotten, then cure what is fitting, and heal the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place with what is appropriate, and suture the place. 
dou chancre	where a sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of a sore, and how one must work on it with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and we say that the sore enlarges in the marrow, and great caution is needed in its cure, and they said the ancients that when a sore is in a place where one can shave it, such as a sore that is on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, one should remove it all when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not right that you approach it, for I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone healed any before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the works, when it is in place or can be removed, as we have said, are that you purge the patient of black bile several times; then make him sweat if he has manifest repletion, then place the patient in a good place to do the work; then shave your ointments or chancres, and all the hair from all sides, and all the bones from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood run out completely, and press the area well with your hand or something else, and if the flow of blood goes against the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with another dressing until it is healed. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the gathering of the water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is erupted only; and one should not touch with iron in these two resemblances: namely tympanites and yposarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this resemblance of dropsy which is called "erupted" with medicines, and the cure does not profit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness than dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the bowels and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient strong of constitution, and he has no other illness than dropsy only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must work thus: lay the patient straight upon your hands, and have the assistants press the belly at the end by putting the water to the lowest part below the breast, then take the spatuumile espinous according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp from two sides. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point and make sure it is not so inserted that it can reach the intestines when you put it in, and you cannot bleeder; then look to see if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if this is the case, you must cut into them with a three-fingered knife right under the nipple; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side of the three-fingered knife; and if it is for the mucilage, it should be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lies on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument and push it through, and lift your hand over the entire spatula between the skin and the syfac as you would when flaying at the quantity of a nail or two; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the eighth place, and this is the place of the sharp point, then pull hard, and push the instrument out. 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a subtle silver cane, and is of iron or light artichoke, and has a small hole in the lower part; and on one side, III holes; and II on another side, and I on another; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision with which writers cut the quill: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Above the head is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, they draw now upon the instrument; empty then half or a third part, for if you empty more than it befits in that hour, by chance he dies because of the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls into palsy, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the sick man signify, and his pulse; then draw the instrument and hold back the point, and it is held now for the heart which opens the pertus which is upon the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin the instrument the next day, if you see the sick man suffering thus, and draw from the point a small quantity; do this every day, and beware of forcing as long as there remains but a prick of a point. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient, and leave a lot of water in them, then treat them with hot sand or burial earth, and with a lot of sweat or bathing in the sun, and let them drink; and treat them with desiccant medicines until they are healed, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after removing the water as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the straightening of the penis 
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it seems necessary as soon as he hasn't pierced all the sputum very subtly according to this form: 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place or pierce a small linen cloth, and bind it tightly for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the cloth and let him urinate, then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes will loosen the closure. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose opening is small, if it is treated with a clove of garlic, as we have said, it will enlarge. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the urethra in its place are blueish, for none are born who have the urethra at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upwards; and they cannot procreate because the matter cannot come up to the marrow, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then extend the head of the penis and the foreskin as the size of a feather, so that the hole is in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding which comes many times, and if it happens, use the one who stops blood, and cure the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis 
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these come upon the penis and are an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are some malignant and some not malignant; so it is fitting that you take them with a delicate lancet, and cut and cleanse all, then put soft cotton on Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the abscess is malignant, of foul color and discharging, then it is fitting that you apply a cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have grasped it, and if the foreskin is over the glans, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the foreskin which is inside first; and when it is sutured, then treat it outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, if you are not sure that the head of the penis is pierced, then blackness and corruption will come in the penis and where it joins; it is necessary to cut off everything that is black and corrupt, then bind an ointment of honey and flour made from pomegranate rind and vinegar on it, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a discharge of blood comes, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauteries help in two ways together: that is to say, in the stoppage of blood, and in corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is fitting that you draw or pull from the penis a leaden cane, and piss the patient among; and when the hairs are burned at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or an abscess, then it is fitting that you scald it with a heated instrument until the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if this is a grievous thing to do, it is fitting that you scald it with a spatula at some point on the head of the penis and the skin; then separate them well, and put a delicate linen cloth moistened in cold water so that it does not burn directly. 
de la circoncision	of circumcision 
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a severance of continuity like the other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our own volition, and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest for safety. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not practice it in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired by experience. 
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the greater part of masters and surgeons who did circumcision around the Nile, and with force, and all with one knife; so it flowed the heart for there are two membranes, and by chance if you cut upon that above and leave that below. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the pain returns doubled, and in the dressing which is made of two cloths, the tip of the limb is not secure; 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the modification which is made to all the length of thread I have found the goodness of experience for the forces cut evenly both above and below. 
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, if you cut equally in I all at once; but let the thread be well twisted around the leather; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only making him tie the thread around the penis just so, and then you can make him rejoice in all the ways you can; then make him leave between your hands straight, and hold the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the children do not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow on it with your heart, and pull it up until the head of the penis is in; then clean it well of the dirt that has assembled there, then tie the place marked with a double thread, then tie it under the other tie; and hold it with two hands by the second ligature to the purse and the index finger, and cut between the two ties, then quickly lift the heart above and pull the head of the penis; then let the blood run little by little, for it is good; and put powder on top and on top of the powder a dressing glued with half an egg cooked tempered with rose water, preserved with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.  
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for mundification is this: the two jaws should be held and sharp, and the jaws should be as large as the handle equally. 
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of mundification is when the heart inside escapes at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your fingernail, just as the pus makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, hold it with tongs, and then cut it. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and what is below the glans is swollen, leave it until the abscess underneath is appeased, and lightly scrape it; if you can move it as you please, and you guard against the part of the glans, it will not harm in any way. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the place of things within a wound with powder, as we have said in our treatise on powders, and if one cuts too deeply beyond measure, and it goes above, it will not harm; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed. 
dou retenement de l’urine	regarding the retention of urine 
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to obstruction of stone, or of congealed blood, or of bowel, or of flesh growth, or of similar things, that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone that is lodged in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent on his knees; and let his feet be placed upon his back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient so that he does not move as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained towards expression of the stone above it, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe," of which this is the form: let it be made of fine silver lightweight like the feather of a bird; and let the tube be a palm and a half long, and let it be slender at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of extracting urine is that you take a double thread and tie the head of it to a piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a stool, and grease his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, as far as it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the buttocks; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and feel the patient's urine coming up to the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless because the one who guides where it goes is crooked; then pull out the thread with all the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and let the urine flow; and start the syringe again until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved. 
des maladies de la vessie	of illnesses of the bladder 
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scalding or blood comes to the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see sharp waters and medicines distilled, then make with all the instrument that is called "clepsydra," and this is its form: 
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the length of the catheter by which the medicine can be such that it plugs the urethra well without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and push when needed; and when you see your medicines in the bladder, put the tip of the catheter into the moisture, and pull on the string that is inside; if you draw the moisture to the catheter, and then push the string firmly inside; if the moisture enters inside, it will come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle enema by which one enemas the bladder: this is it. 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is made of silver or brass and the head is higher; below at the breast or where the liens go; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture that you see to make a clyster, then tie between the two breasts with a good strong thread doubled, and heat the point of this moisture on the fire; then put the head of the clyster into the penis, and hold your hand upon the bladder with all the moisture coming, as long as the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle out of it, and pierce it round about; then put a strong thread into these holes, and join the circle as one joins a dish, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder by pressing with your hand until the moisture comes. 
de la piere	of the stone 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone and its extraction along with medicines; and we have said the difference between a lodged stone and those in the rains, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should operate by incision; and on the bladder, and on the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the sharp pain comes from the bladder resembling sharpness in its subtlety; and it opens wide, and scratches the patient's penis, and it can prick many times, and then hardens; and many of these pains are foundational; and healing is light for children until they are four years old, and it is very grievous for the elderly, and it is moderate for those who are between adolescence and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the phlegm which is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often impedes the search for the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and push and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the level of the bladder, and rises sometimes from its original place; then make him sit between your hands, with his hands below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then seize it and touch it inside. If you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut on top of the stone.  
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not crack at all when touched, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult; and put it in its foundation and seek the stone; and when you feel it with your finger, if it stays at the neck of the bladder; then press on it, and push it out where you see the incision. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then he inserts the speculum cutting, of which this is the shape: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between the thighs and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; and it shall be straight upon the stone, and your two hands shall be at the fundament, and let the waist have a cross so that it is wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perchance if you press with the hand which is at the fundament, it will go out without work.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If then there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must pull it up with the forceps which are also like a file at the head, in order to remove the stone so that it does not escape; or you put under it a subtle curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot insert it thus, widen the hole of the opening, and if the stone is sharp, extract it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, insert the largest first into the neck of the bladder, then pull it up, then cut it loose, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be sewn, and a larger wound made. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For the patient two things happen: either he dies, or his urine comes forth immediately because his veins cannot solder; but nonetheless, you should exert yourself to draw it out, or to tear it apart with forceps, as much as you can draw it out in pieces; and when you have accomplished your work, apply the wound with frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood, and extract it, and put on top a bandage moistened in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then put the patient on his back, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if it rises very well in a place of oil and water, then cure it with diaphyticon ointment and basil ointment until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and urine is held back by it, which is known in such a way that it does not pass with the urine: then put your finger in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and make it rot; then lift the wound with sharp instruments and tweezers, and help it in all the ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is fitting that every hour when you treat it, you tie his two thighs together, and apply medicines on the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is led by the penis, and stuck in, and the urine cannot come out; then the remedy of what I say so, that you cut it many times, is an excuse for the cutting by this remedy. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried this way. 
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron forceps according to this form and let it have three angles fixed in the fire: 
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the trocar into the penis gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the trocar in your hand in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone on the other side; urine will soon come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the penis. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is recently broken and jumps out with the urine, and is painful for the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that stops it, tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then make a rod in place of the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, untie the thread, and clean the frozen blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It sometimes happens that a stone is lodged in women, and if it ever does, the cure is grievous, and is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to uncover herself at the mirrors, even when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is deeper set than the stone of man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessities demand this, it befits you to take a midwife well knowing, and rarely does one find her, and if you do not find one, then take no less subtle a cast; and present her with a wise woman skilled in the lives of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her to do what you command her regarding the inquiry of the stone; and look very well if the woman is a virgin: then it befits you to thrust your finger or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should constrain it under her finger, and recommend that she thrust her finger or hand into the sick woman, and press with her left hand on the bladder formed. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it should be moved gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then place it on the stone in the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the buttock, where it is moved and felt, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her foot above or below the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then put the knife into the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound as much as the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have horns. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the resemblances to know the issue 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood comes, put ground vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the blood is stopped; then return to your work, while the stone is strong, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of the stone from men to help you in your work; and if the blood comes, and it is from the artery which is cut, put powder on the place and bind it with tents and bandages, and do not start again this, and leave the stone and do not pull at it, lest the patient should die by chance; then treat the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the swelling subsides, then return to your work, as long as the stone remains. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia 
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is below the heart of the egg and contains the yolk; and it is called “syfac”, and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks it to be another egg; and it is the skin of the egg between the white syfac that we have said; and this will not peck. 
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is so weak that it comes to the joints, and its matter is spread. 
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never if it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either it is a declining color to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and so on; and these are the signs of knowing this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, it is a returning abscess, I put long as the shape of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the very cloth, then the abscess is rejoined with part of the egg, and because of this one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white sac, then he feels it well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you should examine all the instrument, whose form was described previously. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, which comes after the introducer, judge what is inside. 
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be well bled according to our power and the repletion of his body; then lay him on his back, on something a hand high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and command the attendant to sit on his right side, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the breastbone; then take the scalpel sharp, and cut the skin of the breastbone among them from below up to the nipple, and let your incision be all straight in dividing the skin of the breastbone until the white flesh appears; and pare it subtly according to our power; then pierce the white flesh full of pus with a large opening, and draw out all the pus, and then put on your ointments, and stretch the white flesh upward; and do not touch the heart of the breastbone, but only the white flesh; cut all or in pieces at once its side subtly, that if you do not cut it wisely, it will return with pus; and if the pus comes out forcefully during your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work on the white flesh; then bring together the two edges of the heart of the breastbone with a suture, then treat it as the other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then cut the cord at all the suspension, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the sharp point is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put into the wound linen moistened in rose oil; and put another linen moistened in wine and oil, and put on the two sides, and put doubled cloths on top, and bind it all with a bandage according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and employ wool yarn according to this appearance and let them be assembled by stitching in the throat of the breeches, and one of the points takes upon the fundament up to the back, and the other at the side of the hip; and the other two chiefs upon the two angles, and let all the restraint be assembled in the loop of the breeches; and no medicine is this branch of cautery instead of an iron blade, and it is that you take a sharp surgical cautery and cut the skin of the testicles, and be warmed as we have said so that the white membrane containing the point is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the membrane with one stroke, and scar it with this sharp hot cautery. 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cup in all the ways that you can, so long as you scrape everything; and beware that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and keep guarding against the loss of blood, and milder than the works of surgery; and if anything opposes you, or an abscess grows or there is a loss of blood or other thing, then cure what opposes you, according to what has been said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this procedure because of its horror, then make a perforation as I tell you, and know that when you are quite certain by the signs that we have said that the aqueous humor is there, then have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part across the entire span, making the perforation as long as the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the humor can flow out; then put cotton on the spot and bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining humor, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the humor to escape at the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a quill or the instrument with which one treats the humor in dropsy, the shape of which is shown above, and widen the opening of the wound and know that the humor will return and collect after six months or thereabouts, and when it has collected as before, then the patient will pass their days.  
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles 
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch, fear brings about several situations, for which it seems to me that you would best leave it; and I will tell you the work and the resemblances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and similarly to the testicles; and this is by many causes. 
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known that an abscess arises from excessive sour and sharp humors, which are spread throughout the body, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess follows the color of the body; and there is no pain found, and it is a troublesome abscess; and sometimes one finds a grievous abscess, hard and rough, and dark in color, and at times it comes from a new artery, or swelling of a vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a wound of an artery, it is known by the arrangement of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it is not fitting that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of vein swelling are known by their disposition to the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the incision on this resemblance, and on the other chariots; and it is that you cut the heart of the onions, then raise the egg above, and draw a line through the white syfac, and deliver the suspensory from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the pus is already dried up with these sharp objects, then you must draw out the pus and the cup; and if it is airy in the skin or that which is inside the vessels, then you must deliver all this matter and round the cup. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is or place behind, it behooves that you cut it all away, and extract the egg, as we have said. 
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the thighs 
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering resembling a boil, with the softening of the pus, and the patient groans when he moves; and the cure for this disease is as dangerous as the one before, nevertheless we will tell you its workings according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then put the suspensory from his testicles down to your thighs, to all the vessels which are near the penis, and tie them up, holding the masters, and spreading them out; then cut with a sharp scalpel at a crosswise place through the vessels as long as they are uncovered, and then flay from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then he puts a needle where it has a double thread, and ties it at the first place where the vessel came out, and ties it straight to the other end; then he cuts in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and draws out the corrupted humors; then cure the wound like the others where one introduces the bowel, so that no vessel bleeds which nourishes one of the testicles; for by this there comes no harm, and if all the vessels come visible, it is necessary to draw the testicles to all the vessels; so that the penis does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.  
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the thigh bone 
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this rupture is by section that comes or from a tear, or the stretching above the belly in the part of the groin, for which the intestine descends from this tear to one of the thighs; and this tear is either from the tear, or from the stretching of it, and these two manners come from many causes: either from percussion, or from a jump, or from a brawl, or from lifting a heavy thing wrongly, and by similar things; and the signs when it is from the stretching of the tear, are that it happens little by little, in long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the bottom, because the tear pulls the intestine.  
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a section of the fistula, that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and there are various abscesses appearing underneath the skin nearby, and this is due to the intestine's exit and the body being outside the fistula. 
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never separate the intestines with a knife, and they are held there, and cause great pain to the patient, especially when it is pressed. 
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron out of fear, for which it is necessary to avoid them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.
