And the way of working is such that you instruct the patient to pull the intestine with his hand into the wound, if he can reach it; then be propped up on his neck between your hands and lift the thighs; then extend the heart above, and cut all the skin of the testicles from the length; then put one-inch levers of the waist according to what you need to open the wound, and so that the bones can come out; then flay the white fascia which is below the skin of the testicles, until the white fascia hard is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger in what follows the testicle, in what is between the white fascia which is under the skin of the egg, and the second fascia; and separate what is behind the egg, and between the second fascia; then push with your right hand into the heart of the testicles, and extend the white fascia upward to your left hand, and lift the testicle toward all the fascia towards the waist; and instruct the assistant to extend the testicle upward, and untie what is behind the ligature; and take with your fingers if there is any intestine entangled or white fascia hard, and if you find something, put it in the belly below; then take a needle where it has a large thread made of ten threads, and insert it into the back part of the fascia which is after the skin of the testicles; after the waist, then cut the ends that appear from the threads, until there are four threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the fascia, of which we have said that it is below the skin of the testicles, with a strong ligature of two parts; then envelop the ends of the threads, and bind them in two parts so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter in, so that no abscess comes; and place the ligature according to the first ligature long two fingers from it, and after these two ligatures leave the fascia which is below the heart of the testicles a finger's breadth wide; and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part that is below the skin of the testicles, as much as the sinews and veins, as we have said before; then apply wool moistened with oil, and place it on the wounds, and administer the ligature that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never is it cauterized with white flax as we have said, after the incision, for fear of stopping blood flow. 
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the ligature until it falls out by itself; and if it is delayed in falling, it should be removed with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls out; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia 
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to make the cure by iron. 
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made just as a branch which is joined together with a vine, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision on either side lightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess of the one who operates, until the vessels bleed; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the angles, as we have said, and opens the veins; and no intestines should be drawn out of the joints, and if some are drawn out, it is a bad sign, and it repairs every hour; and nevertheless, if it stays too long in this state, the wound or fistula grows, as long as the intestine is drawn out; and this happens by the extension of the fistula which is at the angles, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and swells the veins and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflamed with a large incision according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the fistula which is below the skin than usual, then take the red-hot iron and put it on the appearing place of the fistula; and press it hard against the belly, then cut the two veins appearing under the fistula on the head of the iron, and cut both; then extract the head of the iron, and do not cauterize the fistula nor stretch the one or the other, as I have told you in the cure of the rupture of intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, let the patient cleanse and care for the wound until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The facial artery is constricted, and there is no visible opening in the wound; the cautery is gentler in this place, and closer to safety. 
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles 
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the cords that are inside are softened, and it is made to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin above the natural skin; then bring together the two edges with a stitch, and if you see, sew first the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and heal like the other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the thread. 
dou chastrement	punishment 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore it would please me not to speak of it in this book; but it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the patient must be able to answer when asked and understand the treatment; and the other is because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that cauterization is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In those that we do by attraction, have the animal sit in hot water, until the tail is softened and drooping; then take it with your hand, as long as they are put back in place and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of size: it is fitting that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut on each egg at one cut, when you have well skinned them; and leave no spot where the syfac or the subtle syfac which are upon the vessels; and this manner of castration is milder than that which is done by attraction, for in attraction there remains perhaps something of the testicles, by which the beast desires luxury; then heal the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites 
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodism is according to two manners like men: one if it appears between the two testicles as the figure of nature of a woman, or if he has hair, and sometimes urinates in front. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another method is for women, and it has on top a dagger as well as a rod and two points. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is such that you cut off all protruding parts and treat them as other wounds. In the second manner, men whose urine escapes through the skin of their testicles have no cure. 
de la tentigene	Of the tenting needle 
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A wen is a fleshy growth added on the natural part, so unsightly to behold; and some women have them as large as a hand, and this is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you hold the superfluity of the tentorium in your hand or on your fingers, and press it lightly; and do not press too hard, lest blood flow, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed; and on another cheek that is born at the mouth of the wound, and apply it, and by chance it jumps out, and according to its appearance like a cow's udder, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease". 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cupping it, as we have said in the previous section, and treat it until it is healed. 
de erratique	Of wandering 
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by illness that has come; or it is by chariot added, or through subtle artifice or species, and it is made perfect in the marrow, or in the ribs, or below, or wherever it may be; and it hinders conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having flowers; and the knowledge of these is by looking at the bail. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the splinters are close together, appearing either at your two thumbs or on your right side.  
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a soft syfac and it is close to the two lips, do this: put your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the two lips as much as possible so that the soft syfac is gone and the swelling subsides; then take wool, moisten it with oil, and place it on the area, and let the woman stay at home each day so she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syphasis is hard and thick, it is necessary that you cut it with a speculum resembling a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stab wound is from a chariot wheel, suspend it with thread and soap; and have medicines steeped in blood, such as agaric, dragon's blood, incense, mixed abundantly with egg yolk; then apply a splint of lead wide enough so that the wound cannot close; and let it remain for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a boil comes, if it needs to be covered according to this manner, unless they are festering boils. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an inflamed abscess which is in the marrow, one should not touch it with fire. 
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids 
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that occur without a rupture and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; and we have said in the division the appearances of others, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and fistulas when they are embedded perfectly in the anus and do not appear to the touch unless it is cured by iron.  
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marshes, one can feel, are those one can cure. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary then that you place the woman in a cold house, and then take the cautery with tongs, and hold it to its roots, then sprinkle powder of medicines which restrain blood, such as alum and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gallnuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it extinguishes, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have them apply cupping to the back and breasts without drawing blood; then take flax, moisten it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the area. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a harsh head, so you must cover it as I said for the thelul; and then treat it until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the sea 
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come in the flesh, such as sores and festering abscesses and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore it is fitting that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that boil; and if you want to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is aggravated at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce, but let it rest until the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a stool, and have two small stools where he can lean, and support himself on his back and bring together his feet at the sides of the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then turn him towards the right side, and he will adjust the instrument with which one operates on the mouth of the abscess, from which the shape will come; and it is fitting that when you see him adjusting this instrument, you should insert the point first to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go any deeper than it should, and so that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is fitting to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is fitting that he put the horn of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and you press it with your hand gently, if it should be covered at its head, cover it with spatumile leaves; and when the bowels are emptied, it is necessary that you place in the wound tents softened in rose oil or in verdigris oil; and put the tent firmly from the wound to the edge of the marsh, and put outside on the marsh and on the handle clean linen softened in water, whether they be cooked or uncooked. Then cure afterwards for two days with anointing suitable to it, until it is healed; and never lift the marsh and the wound by clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lily and long aristoloche that are cooked; then return to anointing.  
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the marsh, it befits you to guard against cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	From childbirth 
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the shape of natural childbirth, and the signs if she sees the woman hasten down, and desire to smell the air: then hurry the child so that it will be born quickly; because when it descends upon its head, the afterbirth comes with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press her belly lightly so that the child is born quickly.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes upon its feet, and the body or the shoulders, and the hands come up, or it comes up on its belly, or often, and is converted by chance off its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its own through natural birth, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a saddle where women hold her; and boil oil or fenugreek, and then pour the broth between her thighs with a small spatula which has this shape: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the second skin and cut to its nail until the moisture that is in it comes out; and take the belly of the woman so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must give the woman a clyster of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil; then make her drink and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: if now the child is delivered. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out forcefully, it is necessary that you gently reset them bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a stool, and raise her feet up high; then overturn the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall during the overturning; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the infant is dead, cut the woman's hands with the knife which has already been placed there, and extract the child, and reset it equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the delivery of a child onto its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, it is necessary to push upward; and then turn it little by little until it is straight; then take it by the feet and extend it little by little. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to the thighs, if he is ordered to take it, and he makes him sneeze from condition; if the jump is strong, if God wills. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, then turn it little by little until it is according to the natural form. 
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light. 
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, say that you take a plaster of aloe, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and defuse this ointment, then make her sit in lukewarm water up to below the ribs; and when she is softened below, give her a suppository of myrrh, and place it below, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and pull out her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child jumps now. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child upon its knees 
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child arrives in this form, if it puts its hands on its chest little by little; then let it be swaddled up to its neck, and hang its feet down, and let it lie on its back off the bed; and fold its hands little by little, and then take its hands and place them on its belly, and remove the cushions from beneath it so that it is fully exposed downwards; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them around, then move its belly upwards, then push its hands up; and lift the child little by little; and instruct the woman to hold onto it as the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the delivery of a child who comes out with one hand extended 
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to try to return the hand: if it cannot be returned, have the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie on the bed and straighten her legs; then administer the muscilage that I have described; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and set the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold herself as long as the child is delivered. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the issue of the child upon its neck, and has spread its hands, and its face turned toward its mother's back 
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is fitting that the patient hold their hand, then turn it little by little and lift it lightly; and when it is equalized, put on the natural muscilage of elder and oil, as we have said, then instruct them to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make them sit on a seat and instruct them to grip; and make them sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same way to all the following  
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes strong in this manner to the whole secondine, so bind the secondine to your finger, as long as the moisture is emptied; and if the child can breathe on its face and on its neck, then bind the child from the elbow, so that it is not held back, and the child dies; then put the child inside as long as you have placed it as it should be, and order the woman to never take hold of it again: then draw it lightly. 
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins 
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens. 
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if you call them names; I know that they should be multiplied, and are delivered by the syfac which devises them, which is tied to the shoulder; and sometimes they issue naturally as all those below, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue grievously, so the cure as we have said, and be the bail subtle, and make quickly and lightly that which it does; and make thus as it is worth moving towards safety. 
de plusors enfans	of several children 
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is fitting that the bailiff knows all this, for if such things happen by chance; then do according to what is right. 
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child 
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound constitution and has no accident or fear of death; it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her hips inclined downward, and her legs raised; and let the midwife hold her down in two places, or tie her to the bed so that she is not thrown about during the delivery of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with a mixture of altea and fenugreek and flaxseed; then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and these mixtures; then gently insert them into the womb; then choose the place where she inserts the ointments to be suitable for this purpose, and take care that if the child is attached it descends on its head; then insert the ointments into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the throat or near the ribs; and if the delivery is on foot, insert them at the heel or side; and it is necessary that she hold the ointment in her right hand, and place the curve between the two fingers of her left hand, and insert it gently with all her hand, and insert the ointment into any of these places that we have mentioned, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the shape of the ointment: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert the other forceps, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then extend them equally by moving them from one side to the other, to make it come out, and let the forceps be toothed to hold it, as this is its form: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, anoint the bandage with some of its oil, and put it into that part, and draw out the other part; and if none remains, put this ointment or higher up, and do this until it all comes out. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other and it cannot be brought back because of tightness, then you must wrap it on a cloth until it is all raised; then apply a cup at the joint of the palm or to the knife, and so you must do with the other hand and the two feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow in its exit, or if it has a sharp point, then you must put the spatumile espinous between your fingers and cut the head and extract the point; or you can grind it with the instrument which is called "almidach," from which form comes with the instruments or chapter which follows this one; and in the same way do if the child has a large head naturally; and then draw the bones with the tongs, and if the head jumps out and is extracted by force, it should be split, as long as the moisture which is in its bad exit goes out; and if it cannot go out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the suction is light, and straightening at the mouth of the breast is light. 
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is three in the belly or breast, it befits that you extract it at the draping wrapped upon the hand; and making the belly or breast, so long as the moisture which is therein runs; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then put the bail of his hand emparfonted from the marrow, and drag it to the mouth of the marrow; then put the oncin one or two, and draw it strong; and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed by a hot abscess which has come therein, then it does not befit to work, but rather administer moist and fatty things; and administer plasters, and seice in acute softening and moistening. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, then follow what we have said about the living child; and if you cannot do so, then treat it in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if he administers what we have said in abscesses which come in the marshes; and if bloodletting comes, it should be put in a sharp restraint, and administer other cures to him. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one child had been dead, then she conceived another upon that one, and the other also died. 
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess appeared on his arm, and it swelled so much that it burst, and he began to have a great discharge. 
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and could not suture the wound. 
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and an bone came out, and after several days another. 
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled greatly, for this belly has no bone. 
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought they were bones of a dead child. 
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wished the wound, and drew out the bones with my hands, as long as the woman was in a better condition; and I left the woman for a long time like that, and there was then a little piece of bone from its place; and I have not remembered this chapter except for this reason, that when masters find a strange thing, they may know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring back the marrow to its place 
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, with which we weigh books; and at two turns are the two heads of the two links. 
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor and made of ebony or boxwood. The mouth should be made of wood one and a half finger widths wide, and the edges of the trees should be one palm and a half long. Between the two limbs there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which should be fastened on one side and the other, a half palm long or a finger more. These two adjustments are placed in the mouth of the marris to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pincers; and it shall have two jaws with two adjustments, as you see, a palm's length long and two fingers wide; and when you see the woman open her vulva for the whole instrument, have her sit upon her bed, feet dangling and legs open, then insert the two adjustments together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs; then work your hand along the whole instrument as you did with the pincers alike, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the vulva, until the woman does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all assembled, and its likenesses are multiplied; and when the master has prepared them, the work is quicker, and higher are the men by their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not prepare your instruments, their necessity is inexcusable. 
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze forcefully, while extracting her hands from her mouth and nose; and if it comes out this way, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole or cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the ulcer, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water on the fire; then put a cane or tube from the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the ulcer, and suck until the vapors go inside the ulcer; then make it sneeze as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second bone jumps quickly. 
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not strong, instruct the patient to wet their left hand in sesame oil or marshmallow mucilage, and then put it into the wound, and want the second one; and when they have found it, grasp it and slowly extend it straight so that the marrow does not break during extraction; but you must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull. Then it will come out and become detached. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the mare is tight and contracted, we have said the cure is sneezing, and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, be careful that you do not go astray; but it is necessary for him who is at the mouth of the mare, that you bind him to the thigh of a woman, then cleanse him with tetrafarmaca ointment; if he recovers and returns, and will come strong; but in any case, when he recovers there will be bad odor in the stomach and head, and it will harm the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is fitting then suitable fumigations for this one: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman to hold back her flowers and her monthly cycle is this: 
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it looks like a cane, and you put the subtle head in the fire, and the wide jaws over the fire; and let there be fumigation over the coals, until the louse is consumed, then begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation 
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but have it stopped up by a subtle membrane; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane with her needle, and not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and she must be careful that she does not touch it; then she puts on linen soaked in wine and oil, and then heals it with ointment until it is healthy. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stay put, put in or insert a cane of lead and leave it for three days, and let it be removed when the child wants to go into chambers. 
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this inflammation comes from the drying of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that dryness: if it is cured, as we have said of the cane of lead. 
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament 
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come below the buttocks are swellings and enlargements that come from near the buttocks or in the space between the two parts; if there is one fistula or more; and when this swelling is old, it works, and still brings forth white pus or thin mucus, and sometimes these fistulas disappear; and they are known by those who have them through discharge or flatulence when the patient defecates, and perhaps by a sudden jump. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that extend to the bladder and halfway up the penis; and they reach the juncture of the thigh and up to the knee. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes the fistula draining at the base, and not draining; and it is that you place your index finger or thumb on the base, and insert a fine needle of steel or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has tortuosity, if you insert a tent of fine flax, or a horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there comes no discharge, neither flatulence nor worm, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hurry in healing. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends as far as the bladder or as far as the urethra, if the urine escapes and cannot be sealed by medicine. 
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced as far as the joint of the thigh, then the tent comes to the place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain surrounds it, then it must be allowed to ripen by itself, and neither medicine nor application by ointment will help; and in these fistulas that persist there is nothing but labor and vanity of foolish opinions that interfere. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those that are not crushed and not old, there is hope for healing with iron, as I have experienced; the patient lies between your hands on their back; and you lift their legs up to their thighs, and bend their thighs towards their belly; then put in a tent of thread or lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the base, you should put your index finger there and then feel if the tendon has been pierced; whether it is uncovered where you feel between your finger the sinew or flesh, then know that it is severed; if one does not work on it, one cannot heal it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One always says that one can heal some well, but this rarely happens; and the help one does is to heat a fine cautery according to the width of the fistula as it has been previously said; and push the whole heated cautery into the fistula until it reaches the bottom. Do this two or three times, so that you know those faulty hairs are burned, which resemble a bird's feather. Then treat with softened bandages in butter, while these hairs are burning, then treat with ointment spreading char and soldering. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is well. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this cannot otherwise be healed; and if the tent is inserted, and does not pierce through to the bone which is its foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or sinew between your finger and the tent; then cut the skin at the beginning of the fistule, and push it forward beyond the tent, and then apply the cautery until it reaches the head of the tent; and the tent will be delivered and fall away; then cleanse those faulty hairs that resemble a bird's feather, and leave none remaining. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood comes, and runs between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine. 
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauteries assemble two good things: that is to say, the burning of these added flesh parts, and the extinguishing of blood and drying of moisture; then the treatment of softened wounds with butter or crushed cabbage, as long as the wound gapes wide, and it is burned into the wound gap; then treat the eye ailment with ointments infused in strong charcoals.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return. 
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes right to the bottom of the foundation, and is far from the body, put your finger or a probe into it and inquire. 
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between II is the cloth or the syfac or chars, where it is near to pierce, if there are no means except by faith and hope, through the administration of one of III ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, put tents and cure as the first; and do not go too far in depth, so that you do not cut the tenement which holds the foundation, and the egestions come through there unwillingly; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and cleanse it once it is cut near the foundation, either by tent or by another pointed instrument; then cleanse that faulty char that is in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula on the part behind the foundation: so it would be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas made in this manner; and it is when you place the tent into the fistula, and it is at the side or near the foundation of the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:  
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I bend the thread into two, and push the tent along the whole thread into the fistula as far as the head. 
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is passing into the margin of the foundation inside, then draw the thread from that hole, so that you moisten your finger or foundation; and pull the end of the thread, and join the two pieces together, and draw one against the other, and leave it for one or two days; and restrain it several times, until the threads catch those teeth which are between them, and they interlock; then cure the wound until it is closed and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, as long as it is not too constricted. 
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make a bandage so tight, then cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spathe which has a spine and from which one makes a fistula is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, for this reason one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here. 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids 
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two manners: or they are within the fundament, just like a grain of resin, and there are small ones and large ones, and they often bleed, and there is one or several, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and still often have a drop of sharp citrine or a drop of blood, and they have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those who have them within the fundament is that you order the patient to abstain so as to go in chambers, until his fundament lets out, so that the threads appear. If you hurry, and it cannot be held with forceps, or you hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots; and if the forceps cannot hold them because of their moisture, take them with a rag, or with cotton, or with a piece of chamois leather; and pull them out with your hands, then cut them off, and powder them with some hot powders which are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot let out, give the patient a harsh and sharp clyster to wash out what is in the fundament, so that it can come out openly; when the patient has relieved himself, and the threads are loosened from the fundament, the cure is easy; and it is that you take them with your fingernail or with forceps, and cut them off, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you administer the suture according to this manner: take a twisted thread and put it in a needle, then pull the thread up above and make the needle pierce through the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be twice as wide; remove the formed thread, then tie a knot in the thread, and remove the needle, and do this for all the others, and leave one to correct the excess blood; then put on the foundation a softened cloth moistened with rose oil or cerate, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; then leave it until they heal, and when they are healed, cure them with ointment and other cures, until they are cured.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the veins or foundation 
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of veins in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use. 
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you place the point of a scalpel or your fingernail on top of the bark, so that it does not become moist; then treat it until it is healed as it should be; and if it cannot heal, start the shaving again more strongly than before, until it heals a lot and is scraped; then treat it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	where it trembles 
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formication is a small false appearance against the body, and it goes very far; and sometimes one finds cold, and one feels it also like death's tremor, and it comes throughout the whole body, more in the hands than anywhere else. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather, and put that cane on the fremit until the circles turn purple around the entire fremit; then turn your hand with all the cane so that you wrap it completely around the fremit, and put it in perfectly, and pull out the fremit by its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this like a chain of iron or steel according to this form, and be slender below and wide above: 
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, but hold it to the pain, and press.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema 
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one gives an enema of silver or artichoke, or melted lead or mallets; and sometimes one uses these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those who are administered treatment for children and those who are weak and painful, are small. 
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema, both small and large, is wide above, where the belly is bound according to this manner. 
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is a separation where the belly is bound, as you see, and the head is pierced within; and it has on one of the sides two holes, and on the other one; and let the belly where one puts medicines be from a beast's bladder or parchment, and be pierced all around with small holes, and let there be between each hole one finger’s space, then put in these holes one strong thread of raw silk twisted in X or some such manner around, and assemble the belly as it were a goat; and when the medicine is within, if you tie it to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then irrigate; and this is the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then insert it gently; then let the assistant hold the patient's two legs together until he is completely still, then extract the clyster, and have the patient lift his legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him strain as much as he can; and if he sleeps all night, it is of greater help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply a clysma for a disease of abdominal flux, and the medicine hastens to pass, then resume it until he is healed. 
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, then let the enema be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of a subtle enema on which the skin is extracted: 
des plaies	of wounds 
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division of the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures by hand and by medicine according to accomplishment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made with, and according to the place or the wounds are made, and by what they are made. 
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Wounds are made by the striking of a stone, and by the edge of a sword and knife, or lance or spear or arrows, or similar things; which are made according to the places in the body, such as a wound that strikes on the neck, or head, or breast, or belly, or liver, and similar parts.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you are careful whether it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt a hot abscess: then make it heal quickly from the cephalic itself if only a little blood comes from the wound, and let it heal on the opposite side of the injured part; and forbid the patient to eat wine and heavy meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal, let his flesh be reduced, and he should not drink wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say a bit later here; and if he has moved it, put on some ointments, until it is healed.  
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like from a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by stitches, then sew them together as I will say for wounds of the belly, with sutures. 
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone and can be held by only a point, then stitch it; then treat the wound with medicine and replace hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat large meats such as haunches and cooked wheat, also pulse, and similar things.
