Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotten flesh, and it does not reach the bone, cut off all the rot, and cast it out, then cure it; and if it has an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be stanched by medicines, cauterize the artery; and if you find it displaced, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light; and it is that you put in this powder which heals as soon as the fire has moved it. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of the powder is this: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coal three parts, and grind the powder subtly, and apply it to the wound, and let it form until it burns well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never is it done with chalk alone, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the fire has cauterized the wound. 
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has burned the wound, immediately put nothing on it; but apply some digested ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it boils; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you about skull fractures later. 
de la plaie dou col	from the wound of the neck 
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut. 
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the cure and not apply anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be below, such as warm-washed chalk in mild water, and mixed with rose oil, and washed cucumber also in mild water, and other stones according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed. 
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is raised and full of pus, then pierce it lower; and if the artery is cut and blood flows, then untie it, ligature it, and cauterize it is necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is kept, by which the flesh goes, then sew the heart onto the cane of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape; and then extract it carefully, and leave it for some days, then cure it with dry ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then scrape it; and if there are pieces of bone, then pull them out all together if you can, and those that you cannot have, then leave them until the wound rots, and is loosened and aligned to the exit; and if the wound is fresh, then powder over the powder that I have said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter. 
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound of lance or knife 
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if wind escapes from the wound while the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal it then with bandages and other treatments as long as it heals; and if it cannot heal, you know that there is a fistula; if the treatment is done as it should be. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from an incision of a sword or knife and it is simple, on the arm or back, then treat the one who is in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, powder it; and if it has penetrated to the bone and has broken pieces, then wash the wound, and remove any foreign objects if they are loose; and if they are not loose, then let the wound fester so that it will lighten the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of tearing of the belly 
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small; from a large wound sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines protrude, which prevents the introduction of others; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because it is harder to put the intestines back in if they are not put back one by one hot; for the intestine swells quickly as soon as it feels cold so it goes back in better, and that is why a medium wound is preferred because you can reposition the intestine to its place as with the other two. And know that a rupture of the belly is according to four manners: the two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the sutures of the other wounds of the body; and two other proper sutures are common to the other wounds; and nevertheless they are more suitable with the suture of the belly, and I will say one by one and declare. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines is outside, and it is easy to put back in place, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen by cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or you cook in lukewarm water squinant and cypress and spikenard, and remove the intestines as long as the swelling is removed; and never do this with restraining wine, for it is milder than that which only serves to reduce swelling. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestines with sharp or high and bad-tasting things that are cooked, for by these the entrance is aligned to little; and if it cannot enter, then make a cut in the wound with an instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure is smaller than the size, so that no one should cut without great necessity nor have it; and this is the instrument for cutting: if you slice inside at the curvature and defur not.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, then put it back in according to its natural form in its own place, if you have power, for this is worth much. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, it behoves that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then put your mind to it so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you should administer what I say in large and small wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, put what has been prepared for you, then hold in your hands the instrument that holds all the stitching together with its hand, and bring the edges together; and this is the common way of suturing, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound the space of two fingers, and put in a needle where there is a good strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the flesh which is under the skin inside, as far as you make it pierce that part, and bring the two edges of the flesh together four together; then draw it tight with a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring the two edges of the wound together neatly, and then leave the space of two fingers, and put in another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to what you need needles, as long as the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be middle-sized, between subtle and thick, because the subtle needles pierce all the flesh, and those too thick cannot enter well: therefore it is necessary that they are middle-sized; and do not push the needles too far beyond the flesh and the skin, lest they pierce and open the wound before the suture; then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and put bandages or cloths on top of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this way of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it allows for one needle or two. The second suture is common, and it is that you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the flesh together with one needle where there is a good strong thread of medium size; and when you have pierced these edges all four together, draw the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner in which we sew clothes; and leave space between each stitch the thickness of a half finger. This suture heals the man, and I sewed a wound on a man's belly or chest, which was cut with a knife, and the wound was more than a handbreadth large, and it was the intestines that were well two handbreadths long, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.  
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I put the intestine back in place after it had been out for XXIV hours, and the wound was sutured up to XV days, and I treated it, and it healed. 
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And those who saw him thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I put only cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and push it from the outer part to the inner part until it goes through; when it has pierced the flesh straight through straight, then leave the head of the thread or twine or whatever you have pushed the needle with, and make it pierce through the other side from the inner part to the outer part; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as the furriers do the furs, and that you leave the thread once on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the whole suture is complete. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is as follows: assemble the two sides together naturally, and apply one end of the sinew to the other end in this manner: insert a needle or the end of a thread nearby, and pierce through that place only, leaving the two ends of the sinew; then turn the needle and pierce it from the outer side to the inner side, along with the two ends of the sinew; then pierce both sides from the outer side to the inner side, in two other ends of the sinew which are on the other side; this is the simpler way of stitching and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and no one contradicts it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in it; and one must put one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew belts; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more painful than others in the sides of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of the other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, so that the fire has moved it, then put back to air the intestine, and the cut; then put on top the powder of roasted charcoal, and if the fire has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound boils; and stitch the thread, and let the sifac, and the mirach be soldered; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on it, as soon as it begins to boil and swell, old cotton, and stir it twice a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in several positions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will cause commonality to the principal members, it is fitting that you moisten linen slightly in tempered oil, or in rose oil, and place it around the embers, and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or decay in the bowels, which often happens, then give enemas of warm red wine, and similarly if the decay comes up to the intestines; and pierce within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is lighter to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the arrangement of its veins, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the arrow jumps from the wound, put it back in place as you would the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you must bind the area that is black so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the binding, and suspend the two ends down from the part below the wound until it comes out to align the extraction when the arrowhead leaves, and the wound opens. 
de la routure dou boueil	Of the fracture of the eye socket 
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, if one can restore it in some men, for I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it was stitched up and became a fistula, and from it came the excretion and windiness; I put care according to what I could, and did not cease to subtlety until he was healed, and his intestines were joined. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sutured, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he did not have any pain, but remained in better condition, and ate and drank; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in this manner: take flax with large heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the flax has opened its mouth, put it on the two lips so that it tightens its mouth on them; and then cut off the head, and this will hold so that it cannot be untied, then put another flax afterward in the same manner as before, until the wound is all closed up; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If these heads catch fire in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the head of this intestinal thread that is well stripped, then tie to the head of this thread a fine linen thread twisted tight, then pass the thread through the needle and sew the intestine and close it at the rupture; and this manner of sewing for trembling intestines is nothing more than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the intestinal folds, there is no remedy or healing except subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or where it may be 
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes old, is called universally "fistula," and the same when it is healed and returns inward. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the greenness, a hard and white nodulation, where there is no pain felt, and it is also raised like the feather of a bird; and sometimes in a clear bow, and sometimes thick; sometimes a spot, and sometimes enough; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only due to one of the nine causes: namely, by the smallness of blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the edges, which does not allow flesh to grow; or because there is too much pus; or because the wound is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or because the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow to digest, and slow to heal, and swollen by nature; or because there are veins or bones; and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore, it is fitting that I make you aware of the treatment of fistula which is done by handwork. 
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body; for there are fistulas which come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the facial bone, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of difficult healing, and there is nothing else but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come up to the place I have said, and you are confident of the cure, and you see it known, then take a tent of linen or iron, if the fistula is straight, if you want it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not bother you or the principal members as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, remove all the decay until it is entirely gone, then treat things that generate flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns back in the same way as before, know that you have not yet reached the end: uncover and scrape until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that corruption is too advanced, and you cannot proceed; there is nothing to do but leave it to nature; and if there is only a small bone corrupted, and you can grasp it with forceps, extract it with an appropriate instrument for this purpose; and if there are many bones, treat them all, leaving none behind; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut through the flesh, bone, and char, and free the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something promoting decay on the wound and leave it until the flesh is rotted around the bones, then you will be able to remove the bones more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as one of the leg or thigh, let the corruption continue only until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part that has become corrupted, and it comes up to the marrow of the bone, you must sew and cover it all the way to the corruption, then cure it until it is joined; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example from it and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about thirty years who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the humors went to the leg, and it swelled into a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the midwives, through their folly, worked so much on it that they opened the abscess, and corroded out many humors, and it became a fistula, and there came many pores that all discharged pus and moisture from the body; and many midwives treated him for about two years, and he had no wise man in the healing arts, until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what ran out through the pores into a large container; and his body became red, and he had a yellow complexion. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent into one of these holes, and then I closed all the holes, and I found that some came against each other from all sides of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a portion of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption extended to the bone inside; I removed what appeared to me of the corrupted bone and thought there was no other corruption, except for that which I removed; and began to restore the wound with medicinal sodas for a long time, but could not solder it; and then I started again and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued into the bone, and removed it, and tried to solder the place; but I could not until I cut around a palm of bone, and applied the treatment to all its marrow, then I restored it with medicinal herbs; and it healed and soldered quickly, and it was no longer necessary to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For bloodletting often causes bleeding, but it was healed completely, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and was well-disposed and had no harm nor contradiction at all, neither coming nor going. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a linen cloth and bind it to the head of the bone which appears, and command someone to stretch it upward; and put another woolen bandage larger than the first bandage, and tie it above the flesh that is below the bone, and extend the head so that you draw the corrupted flesh beneath, and uncover the flesh on the place where you wish to solder, so that the solder does not burn the flesh; and put a burning ember or a plank underneath the bone to melt the corrupted flesh; and it should be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and treat it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, uncover all the flesh; then put the ember underneath, and then solder from one part to the other the corruption, and let the soldering be as long as the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, solder the corrupted joint, and solder the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy than to solder; and if the corruption is at the point of the hand or the point of the foot, it is very serious, but nevertheless it is necessary that you inquire into this corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not oppose you; and know that there are many instruments for soldering these bones according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of them, their thickness and subtlety, their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each semblance of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of the diseases; so consider the instrument which you need according to what it requires. 
dou feu	By fire 
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder can rot from within or from without; and when you have medicine to corrode that by the treatment of medicines, and it does not profit, then it is necessary to cut off that limb up to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or from the malice, which is greater, of the loss of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it appears as if it were burned by fire, and rots after the blackness, since the corruption goes from limb to limb, and takes hold of the whole body; if you hasten in cutting off, and if it is by the sting of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar creatures, if the corruption is at the head of the arm, then cut it off, and do not give it space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, bind it at the joint so that the gangrene does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, bind it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and do the same when the gangrene comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, bind it after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, bind the whole foot; and if it rises to the leg, bind it at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, cauterize the area immediately, or apply some astringent powders. Then return to your medicine until it is complete, and then bind the injured limb tightly with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his left foot: he developed a blackness that looked like a burn from fire, and this corruption first appeared on the back of his left foot, spreading until it affected the entire foot. When the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cauterize his foot, and it was healed; but long afterward the corruption returned in the back of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied counter-irritant substances after cleansing his body, and was unable to stop the corruption; and he asked that I cauterize his hand, but I refused, for I had hoped to counteract the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because the man's strength was weak. The man despaired entirely, and returned to his home, and hastened to cauterize his hand himself, and it was healed; and I have told this story only so that others may do likewise if they need to. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in fleshy place, and stays so long that it gathers a great deal of pus; and then it bursts and the pus flows out, and the sore remains open, like a vessel; and the skin on top is as thin as a delicate linen cloth, and does not extend to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such sickness is called "healthy," and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin, if you cut it all around, even when it is thin, like linen; and does not spread because of its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have confidence that the flesh will burn and the corruption is not perfect, and the flesh is thick like leather, do the cure of an enema as follows: look to see if the breast is large, and the bowel that comes from it has a foul odor, then enema with Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take alum, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them to cook in a vessel over fire until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and make an enema into the breast and extract the pus; and leave the medicine in place for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed and the foul odor is removed.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is in perfect condition, do not allow char to be generated there; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see it, arrange it in such a way that the bowel runs down to the lowest place where it is. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast swells and is indigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal. 
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair of health at all, for health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose wounds heal slowly, and some who heal quickly; and if a hard lump remains in the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing; and if the breast is slow to heal and is swollen, apply drying medicines, moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as diachylon ointment, for there is a great deal of vitriol in it, and it is the last medicine. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger 
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A boil is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or by chance arises in other places; and when it is envied, and no attention is paid to it, it comes a large abscess, running and carrying pus so much that it runs down to the root of the nail, and by chance runs all over; and corrosion comes up to the bone, until there comes foul pain, and the flesh of the place becomes wide, and its color red. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluous flesh which has remained from the wound, then cauterize the wound afterwards. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauteries are of great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and begins to grow in and bleed, then you should put a ray under the nail that pierces the flesh and push it up, and cut this flesh subtly and lightly, and put medicinal burning and corrosive substances on the remaining flesh to remove all of it. Then cure it with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it and treat it hard, for as long as the corrupted bone is there, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone corrupt, cut it in one of our ways as mentioned before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is hard and swollen, and he feels great pain, you must first heal it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula by cutting across above it, and be careful that the cut does not go down to the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on it that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the deafness of the hand 
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two fingers which are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is a part where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in some us of the two. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those born without any pain in the shoulder do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the shoulder sometimes move; the size of one who is fleshy should be light, in a certain way: cut it at its root with a broad spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is grief to cure: if you hold him tight. 
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must be delivered soon, it is necessary that you cut around the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone with a saw suitable for this, and then heal it until it is healed.  
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The weldings that come to two together come by birth, or by welding of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things. 
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is fitting that you bind this suture so that the bone may repair according to its natural shape; then place between two bandages or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not fuse; or you may place between two pieces of fine wood until the bone is fused as it should be. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of his limbs with the palm, so apply that bandage as it should be. 
des vils	of old 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large vessels wrapped full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many members of the body; and they are more common in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer to him a purge of coles, and then the juice of basil. 
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is that you cauterize them and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you open the vein and treat it all thoroughly. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The setting is according to this manner: first raise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the fat becomes thin, then pull the leg from the patient above the thigh up to the part below the knee; then cut a vein in one place or two or three places, with a wide incision. Then draw and extract black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can bear; and then bandage it, and order him to abstain from meat eating black garlic; and start again the evacuation and the purging when the veins are full, and harm the patient.  
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the arrow is according to this manner: Take the leg of the patient, if there are a lot of hairs, then put it in a bath, and apply hot water to the leg until it becomes red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire and then apply the place where the vein is long at the top of the knee or in the part below the ankle; then cut the skin with a knife, and flay the vein on every side until it appears when it is touched, and it is seen red and black, and when it enters into the skin it seems as white as a rope; then put the arrow underneath until it is raised from the skin, and then pull it up to the knife slightly, then apply it in another place three finger-breadths above; then flay the skin on the vein until it appears, then lift it with the arrow as you have done, and pull it to another knife as you have done first; then apply another incision or more if you need them, then lift it, and apply it to the toe, then draw and lift it up to the second incision; then extract it from incision to incision until it is entirely out, then apply it; and if you cannot draw and lift it, then put a strong double-threaded needle under it, tie it and draw it; and then put it under the arrow, and turn your hand on one side and the other until it comes out; and be careful that it does not cut, because if it cuts, you cannot draw or lift it and it will be harmful to the patient; and when you have drawn it all out, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wound together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly but do not sever it completely; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one cuts the vein if it is curved, and does not cut, then it cuts the vein; and it is of a large curve, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the form: 
de la voinne civile	of the civilian vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is engendered in the legs, in warm parts where neither herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this comes from the putrefaction that comes under the skin, as it comes within the body snakes and worms, engendering between the skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to come out, just like a root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder joint is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of linen from three and a half to eleven and a half fingers long, and tie a knot, and let the linen hang down the leg, and every time that there is pus coming out, wrap it around the linen again, and tie another knot; and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, as long as it is all coming out.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never at this vein only two times, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot or hand, and much pus comes out, and from which it springs; cure it then as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms which are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "ox disease", because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and the one who has it feels it well from limb to limb, as long as it runs under the skin where it goes, and jumps further; and it comes from the corruption of certain humors, as come worms and serpents and lampreys and roundworms or bellyache; and we doubt its malice, for when it goes through the body, and rises to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance enters in, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cleansed and milked, one cannot remove it except when it goes: so it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong cord tightly, then cut on top and milk it hard, and if the worm is fully embedded in the flesh and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the eye, remove the eyebrow below it, then cut on top and milk it hard; and it is necessary to treat the patient with cleansing of the body with dissolving medicines for bad rotten humors, and beware of food that causes rot. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain which comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This sickness is called "vacarir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and can move from member to member; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed her arms to me, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as a worm on her shoulder, faster than anything else, like living silver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and went into her shoulder, and then a moment later ran throughout her body, until it reached her other arm; then she told me that it was now turning around her body, just as I saw it. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner. 
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had indeed wanted to move pain from one place to another, but I had not wanted it myself, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, and therefore appeared that constrained windiness; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see curing this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then bind it above and below hastily, and then cauterize on top until the wind constraint in place is forced out; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it at your eyes, then cure with those who expel winds, such as fetid pills, and serpent pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge. 
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are some which have large points, and small ones, and bearded ones, and soldered ones; and those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those in which there are pieces; and the one which falls into any member falls according to two manners: either into a principal member it falls, such as brain, heart, liver, lung, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.
