When the arrowhead is thus in any part of these limbs and the signs of death which I will tell you hereafter appear to you: then it behoves that you should abstain from extracting this arrow for death comes afterwards in many dispositions; and when these evil signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, treat it and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow hits and pierces the bone, and leaps the dura mater which is above the brain, is when there is scotoma and numbness and vertigo and redness in it, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is discharge without odor from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there comes moisture from the wound white looking like a poultice, and it leaps also as if burned with fire; and if these signs appear to you, then take care of the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not inside. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of a heart attack when it occurs is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the heart also moves like a pulse, and black blood comes forth, and there comes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: know then without doubt that death follows. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never left the wound is that without pus it leaps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs heavily and desires cold air. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if an arrow lodges in the covering of the buttock, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great suffering and sighing; and it moves all the members of the shoulders. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow sticks in the stomach, by chance some undigested meat may come out of the wound. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow lodges in the gut or the stomach, and there is no passage through the intestines, there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow lodges in the bladder, and the urine jumps and comes out burning, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the shoulder blade and the spine of the back and the forearm and the thigh and the legs, and similar members, are safe according to various positions. 
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me so that you do the same. 
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell or slipped into the root of his nose; I tried it and drew it out from the other side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any harm. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he pulled out an arrow with a game that had fallen into the fat of the eye below the skin below, and the arrow was feathered, and could only reach the point towards the fire, and it was a large arrow like a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the player was healed, and no evil accident came to him. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I removed an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with fletching: I shaved the beard, and I worked subtly until I removed it, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I removed an arrow from a man who had it lodged in his belly and thought he would die; and then after thirty days he did not change position at all; I cut upon the arrow and hooked it, and removed it, and he had no bad consequence. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man into whom an arrow has fallen or gone in, and the wound has healed over it; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position, nor finds harm in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man, to whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sewn shut; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I drew out an arrow from the nose of the king, who was fallen into it halfway, and it was leaning a little to the right side; and the arrow was all buried. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I put it all to the test with great subtlety, and I did not feel it at all; and he felt numbness and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of an arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for four days, and sewed up the wound right away, and kept the patient like that for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his flesh; and he told me so. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put corrosive medicine on the wound for several days until it was open and tested it, feeling the head of the arrow rise to its place; then I added more of that corrosive medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and within four months the end healed well, and then I widened the wound so much that I could put in the forceps, moving it from one side to the other, and it would not come out; then I did not stop refining and devising instruments in various ways until one day I took it out with well-made forceps, according to its form which will be shown at the end of this chapter, so that I extracted it and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the master surgeon judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure on what I do not say, for books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters compare themselves to a very small thing, and to what is present and lacking, they find nine works, and nine instruments, at the descent of foreign things which happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not leave the limbs where they are stuck except according to two methods: either through the place where they enter or through another part; and the one that is removed through the place where it enters is an arrow entered into their flesh, and is rarely removed now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh is rotten around it, and the way out is clear; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce around it with a fine awl, until the flesh around it is enlarged, and then extract it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: then do not draw it out, but leave it until it is equal after several days, for if the arrow comes as far as the sinus, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed in more than just the bone, and it does not reach as far as the sinew, and the patient remains for a few days without bad accidents, then draw it out with an engine. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck like this and cannot come out by force, then administer poultices around it, as I have told you; then heal the area until it is healthy. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that you cannot see it, if it has all of its fletching; and if you can feel it, draw it out with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then widen the wound so that it is large; and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it holds, remove the flesh which is stuck to it on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can draw it; but be careful not to break the arrow so that you would draw it more grievously. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding flesh has rotted, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood is against you, apply what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting a nerve or vein, and place whatever you can to draw out the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow fell upon him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes in from another side, or where it appears nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place so that one sees it or feels it apparently: cut then, as much as the pliers can grasp, and then extract it; if it jumps now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out. 
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out forcibly; and if there were an arrow there, push it in all the way through; and if it were bone, and you see that it must be pushed, administer the instrument with its point facing down, so that the point of the arrow enters into the groove of the instrument; and then push forcibly, and if the arrow is raised, push the instrument in with the point entering inwards to ease the extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as is fitting. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow lodges in the flesh or chest or belly or bladder or side, and it is close to the surface, and you can grasp it, then grasp it; and be careful not to grasp the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then suture the wound if necessary; and treat it until it heals. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs with which we treat arrows is like the beak of a bird, and see here its form: 
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the end of the arrow is like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, as this is the shape: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tongs for pushing and for knowing if it is this: 
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body 
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one can be bled, of which there are XVI on the head; to wit: II batans which are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the II arteries which are in the II temples apparent; and II veins which are in the II corners of the II eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein which is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein which is on the top of the head; and the II guindeges which are at the neck; and the II veins which are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins which are called "augeherich"; and II veins which are below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins which are commonly used for bloodletting are three in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and common people call it "the vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fascia," and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and common people call it "the vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side, and common people call it "the vein of the belly," and it is above the fossa, and it is the one we use for bloodletting, which appears clearly on the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvation vein is the one that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the pocket on the left side, and the second is a saphenous vein that is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The vein of the temples behind the ears helps against old catarrhs and migraine; and the quality of the bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the neck of the patient to a screw, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two strands hanging from the head: then press them with your finger, and wherever you feel the pulse below your finger, mark it; then take the lancet and push it under the vein until the bone; then lift your hand along the whole vein upwards and cut both the skin and the vein well in two directions, and let blood flow out as much as you see; then bind and bandage it until it heals. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for an old headache, and a chronic one, and a customary ophthalmia, and for the body of sharp tears as it were; and the quality of the bleeding is as I say: and it is that the patient tightens his neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and he puts his thumb under his collarbone, and then presses with his index finger; then lifts the heart up on the vein in high at your thumb index, and puts the lancet below, and lifts the vein upwards, and cuts it as you have done in the other two veins, and let blood flow according to your necessity; then loosen the patient, and put your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of them, and their cutting, and their extraction, at the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting of the cephalic for diseases of the face that are old, and migraine, and redness. 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see; then untie the patient's neckband, and tie the vein tightly so that it is clean and never again opened with a wide blade. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not fitting that the flame be too strong; and cut across, for the bone is close by, and by chance break the flame when it is subtle. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting of the two veins that are in the two temples helps with those things, and with tinnitus, and with redness, and with inflammation in the eye, and with illnesses of the face; and the quality of their bloodletting is such that the patient twists his neck with some kind of bandage, as before; then he bleeds, and let the bloodletting be either a deep cut, a long one, or a wide one.  
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, it may break; then make a dressing of blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein of the nose is good for ague, and strong feverishness, and illnesses of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, even when it is old; and the quality of the blood is such that the patient constricts his neck, then strains his nose in your left hand, and takes a long, subtle flame, and puts it between the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well unless you do so, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too far into perfection, and let two bloods flow according to your need, then bind it one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The vein of the two temples helps in the constriction of the bladder, and at the beginning of measles, and for many diseases, and for impetigo, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and for estiomenes; and the quality of the vein is such that the patient draws his neck under the one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then cut the vein along a wide space, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as needed; then redo the same in the other vein, then loosen the tie, and release all the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave him until morning, so that the wound is healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	From the health of the liver 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The veins of the lips above help to glue in the mouth, and to corrupt gums, and fissures of the lips, and teeth rot and decay. 
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the vein is to have the patient sit in front of you, and pull their neck as I said; then turn back the lip, and look for the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that small black veins surround them: so take both, and if you don't know them, and you are in doubt, take the largest of each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the vein under the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The vein bloodletting under the tongue helps after the cephalic bloodletting, and it is for constriction of the throat, and eye diseases, and mouth diseases; and the quality of the bloodletter is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black vein: bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for below are arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins through which we commonly heal are healed in two ways: either by pricking with a sharp flame or a very fine olive-wood instrument like cutting needles, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the burning mirror is much renowned and is wide as you see: 
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins that are full of thick blood visible, and which contain thick and muddy blood; and this is the form of olive oil. 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle pointed, and it is for lancing subtle veins, where there is thin yellow blood. 
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are below the throat, and at the neck, and at the chest, and at the belly; and it is necessary for the healer to bleed it well, and to wash from the artery that is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it severs the artery and bleeding comes, then you must cauterize it as I have said; and the flame should not be pointed but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, it is necessary that you extract it and change another; or if you want any vein of it, or you put in its place the vein under the arm: it opens manifestly; and apply the cup to the flame as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the location of the vein, it is necessary that you remove the arm, so that you touch the location until you know the pulse; then mark the location with a bandage and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a lancet cauterized in flame; and be careful not to wound the artery when you see the inflamed place because it is the artery: avoid it then.  
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protrude at the top as urine from a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: hurry then and place your finger on length, and then remove your finger if the blood stops; many times this happens; bind the arm then and leave it like that and do not move it for the patient; be without fear and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stemmed, and it flows to you, and the medicine is not present, then bind the artery if it appears, for the head of the vessel will retract; and stem the blood. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a bark of fig and cut it, and take one half and tie it well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, cure it as we have said with powders that stop blood; and the stopping of the bleeding is not bad in several positions because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the bandage on the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle aids so that it draws blood from above the head and below the body, for which reason it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic as we have said; and it behooves the healer to beware of the nerve that is beneath, and if he points too far and finds the nerve, it will swell and the wound will fester, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve appears much more often, and if it does not appear in some men for its subtlety, then you must use an instrument to loosen the nerve. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then make the incision long. 
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the cephalic is so helpful that it draws blood from the head and helps them; and one must bleed by pricking at the olive flame or the myrtle flame, for it is the safest of all veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery beneath it.  
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is best to seek the lightest place, and do not worry if it fails the first time, and you start again; and by chance the limbs swell in some men when it fails the first time, but it does not matter. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your thought. 
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is not administered except to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses; and let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins which are: cephalic, basilic, and fasting; and it should be done at the beginning of spring for young people, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first day or the third, after two hours or three of the day. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The saigne which is administered to the sick has no determined hour, but only when need is of day or night, in all hours and all times; and it does not behoove to bleed children until XIV years, nor a woman carrying a fetus beyond the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Those who have passed sixty years should not be bled. 
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be blooded, in whatever way it may be, it is fitting that he should cleanse his bowels with a light clyster, if he has retained much phlegm, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines harmful superfluities damaging the principal members; and no one who is too full of meat, or drunk, to the point of being forced, or dropsied, should be blooded; and one should not blood after a colic passion, vomiting, flux of the bowels, and multiplication of intercourse with a woman, and labor, watching, and fasting, and those whom all virtue has left, or by some thing from the weapon or body; then subtly the humors, if he is fat, by food and drink and medicines, if you have the power to procure them; then enter into a bath, if nothing forbids it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the left arm around the third hour, as we have said; and keep yourself on that day from work, and exertion, and luxury, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and let the bleeder be higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then loosen the ligature moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot hold the blood; and then rub the place with his hands until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the bleeder’s thumb with a drop of old oil, then put his left hand finger on that vein beneath the place one fingerbreadth from where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not move and fail when struck.  
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee as cords in the body, and if some are full of windiness, so that when you apply fire, it withdraws from the fire and cannot open the vein, then one is like this; and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for this reason it is necessary that the surgeon be warned in these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein works the first time, that is good; if not, start again a little lower than that place or higher quickly, if the veins are not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the arm is swollen and the patient is afraid, leave it for one or two days, and do not bandage the arm: for fear it may develop abscesses; nor bathe in it, then begin the lancing again if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or the sinew subtly, and you doubt that it will not issue as much blood as you see, thrust into that wound itself all the flame directly; and perform a hastening puncture so that the arm is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not start the bleeding again, and put a poultice of oil on it, for it relieves the body of blood, and the oil mixes with the poultice in this place; and thus administer the oil poultice in every vein that you bleed, to stop the flow of blood; and the same does triacle and wormwood, when it is put on the place; if too subtle the poultice, it separates when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess should develop, which often happens even when the vein opening is small except for the time when blood is being drawn, then hurry and put on the area a sponge moistened with hot water and vinegar, and leave it there for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has been drawn from the vein. And if it stays in place after several days without any blackness or greenness, do not harm it; and if you see, put on some aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, monsterwort, or something similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there arises an abscess and swelling in the vein of the arm; put your hand on it, then if you find the place soft under pressure from the hand, that swelling is bad. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not put anything on any of what we have said, for fear in cutting it will hit an artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place and then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.  
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood. 
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for one who is strong and robust, and needs bloodletting, that a wider incision be made, and the lancet be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be bled frequently in small amounts, and he must be bled by cutting across, not by piercing; and this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive bleeding and damage to nerves, and is worth more than a long or wide incision. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body lacks nourishment at the time of healing, it is fitting to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is hot, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of cold complexion, give him before the healing softened bread in thickened syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a fragrant syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after the flow of much blood, it is fitting that he inhales broth of flesh and subtle fragrant syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of veins. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to strengthen his arm, and bleed again, it is fitting, when he is weakened by a large bloodletting, that he bleeds a little at a time, according to the amount of his strength continually. 
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to cauterize their arm after the first incision, and they have strong flesh, then they should cauterize seven hours after the first incision, or after the ninth hour. 
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And he who wants to heal from another part, it must heal on the second or third day. 
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has much blood within the body which is already heated, and brings fever; so it behoves to draw forth a great quantity, and enlarge the opening so that it flows freely like a stream; then after you have attended to all the conditions of health, and put your hand upon his pulse when he is healthy, so that death does not come in place of healing, which often happens when the healer is negligent; and it behoves not when you see the arm untied, and make the blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press hard upon it; nor if it is crooked, that he stretches out the arm hastily, for this would be bad; but let him keep it as long as it heals the second time; or put a burning coal at its point, so that the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein flows freely, and put upon it a piece of silk made sharp, and press lightly. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed. 
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, if the vein in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm. 
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein beneath the arm is cut in place of the head vein because it is composed. 
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient plunges their hand into hot water, until the pulse is red; then it is tied moderately so that the vein appears well, then the bloodletting is done now across, not broad nor long; and the opening should be wide, and the bloodletting done very close to the joint of the hand, and if no blood can come out, the patient puts their hand back into hot water, and lets the blood run into the water until they have enough; and if it is summer, do not plunge the hand back into hot water, for one puts it in more in winter than in summer; and the bloodletting of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are neither artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sinew of the salvation of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and plunge it into hot water, as long as the vein is swollen, if you see it; and if the sinew is across, and if you cut it in every part, it does not grieve anything; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath all bare of flesh, and then put the hand back into hot water, if the sinew is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is needed, put oil and silk on the vein to heal quickly, and do the same for every wound. 
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sinew of the hand in the left is worth as much for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you on the right. 
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The vein of the sophene is worth more than all the diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the thighs and legs old, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his remedy is such that the patient puts his bare foot in hot water, and rubs it on the vein until it bursts, and ties it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and runs up the foot with many veins; so heal either a larger vein, or one at the ankle, which is better. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cauterize it on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are underneath, and cauterize it through as in cutting; and let the flame be numb. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back into the water, and let the vein drain well. 
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the sinews fail the first time, begin again a second time above a bit, for the flesh is salty; do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and so do to the sinew of the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The sinew of the sciatic vein is at the ankle bone, and its pain extends to the hip, when it is due to hot blood. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his vein is such that the patient must enter or bathe, and twist four times above the ankle, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, pull the vein in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is worth more to draw it than to cut it, for the blood is beneath, and it is very full of hands. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, so healthy any vein of his that opens or on the back of the foot, and towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves; and make as much flow of blood as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put cotton on top and remove it; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	from cupping glasses 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horns, or gourds, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding. 
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventosation which is done without iron is according to two manners: either it is with all fire, or without fire; and ventosation which is made by striking and by extraction of blood is made in fourteen places on the body, of which one is all at the top of the head; and the others are below the neck; and two others on the sides of the neck; and the cupping glass below the chin; and the cupping glass on the two shoulders; and the cupping glass on the buttocks; and the cupping glasses below the two arms; and the cupping glasses on the two legs; and the cupping glasses on the two ankles; and the ventosation does not draw blood, except for small veins which are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken one at all, as one does when drawing blood from a vein; and it is not right that it be administered, neither with all fire nor without fire, in any illness which comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity of illnesses requires cupping, or for customs, if we apply it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and midday and every time; for there are some who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and there are some who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in them; and there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and spit blood; and there are some who faint, and see by night blood and sadness and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is less than a month old, we order him to be cupped after three hours of the day. 
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sinew of the thigh helps the headache... which comes from them, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosation is in place of the sinew of the cephalic, and it is not fitting that he who is of cold complexion use it, or who has diarrhea, for this does them much harm; and for this reason it is not fitting that the elderly use it, nor those who have head colds. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover often become oblivious, so it is necessary to place the cupping glass a bit lower due to the fear of oblivion. 
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Ventosation applied to the neck is in place of the sanie vein and the basilic vein, and for this it is worth for the constriction of the bladder, and for the fissure of the canal of the rectum, and for all other things; and one must not press too hard, because if it holds too firmly, it will cause obstruction or stomachache and heart problems. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping at the second ribs of the neck is good for headaches, ophthalmia, migraine, strangulation, and pain at the roots of teeth; it is placed on the line of the basilica vein; and you must instruct the patient to press his hand down on it so that he does not cut an artery and blood does not flow. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping below the chin is good for mouth disease and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; it is also in the place of the sores of the two lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping of the shoulders is good for illnesses that come from heat and swelling. 
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventosations of the thighs are worth as much as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient that he should not make too deep a drawing, because the flesh is naked of fat, and beneath lie nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass which is on the croup is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases below, and it is fitting that the cupping glass be large and be of iron so that it has need to draw well; and by chance, if it were thin, it would break; and it makes large wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	If the cupping glasses on the legs bleed freely, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the loins, and bladder, and soften tumors; and they are placed in the location of the two thighs, and the two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring paleness in many conditions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is that you put it first empty and suck slightly and put it hastily and move it evenly and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen and appear the redness of blood; then remove and put back the cupping glasses, and take care in the disposition of the bodies because there are some who have thick flesh and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike once only and make wide wounds and a deep one and suck slightly.  
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it is fitting to cut it twice: the first time to make subtle the way of the thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is fitting to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out blood little by little, we only strike once. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we begin often; and if the blood is thick, we pierce it deeply, and the ends should be such that the heart is pierced frequently; and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have large pores, that you moisten the places where the cupping glasses will be applied with oil that is stimulant and dissolving: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or balsam, or aniseed oil, and similar oils. 
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if he whom one treats has tender flesh and large pores, it is not fitting to put any oil on, but rather one must wash after the cupping with rose water, or cold water, or nightshade water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or other similar. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should get up with ash, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things. 
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities should rise from old wine, or vinegar, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not suitable to apply a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping, and he should wash himself both when he is about to be cupped and after he has been cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard against those who are recovering from anger, and if the wound is too hot and inflamed; it is necessary that they take cold things, such as pomegranates and endive and lettuce in summer, and similar things; and eat little, and goat meat, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should take syrup of honey and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and eat little, and eat few and small birds and pigeons; and on the day they will vent themselves, they should drink more than eat; and it is fitting to give some men triacle or musk before or after venting, to strengthen the principal limbs; and let the sans be subtle but it does not fit for those who are hot to drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are applied without wounding are those that are applied on the liver, and on the bladder, and gout, and on the stomach and the arm and the thighs and the hip, for these limbs do not suffer to be wounded at all, and it is only done for the purpose of drawing blood from one member to another, just as we put them on the breasts when a woman does not bleed; for removing the viscosity that is in the member, just as we apply cupping glasses on the stomach and on the arm to reduce the member; and removes pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue by chance the obstruction, or detaches the stone from its place; and so it does when it is applied on the liver and on the bladder when there is retained windiness, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of hot water, just as in diseases of pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been boiled. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is thus: 
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two fingerbreadths wide and half a palm long, and it should have a small hole in the middle, like for sticking a needle through, and made of horn, sharpened beforehand so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and it should have a crossbar in the middle, made of horn or iron, to put a candle holder on, and they should be large and small according to the illnesses and age of those who use them; for children's cupping glasses are different from those of old people, and those of thin people are different from those of fat ones. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must put this suction cup onto the limb: take a candle of wax or linen thread and put it in the suction cup through the stem which is in the suction cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and your two hands must be on the opening that we have said, so that when you want to see if it goes vapor, and take off the suction cup; and take the linen thread as before, and start again often, if you need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered in sickness of pleurisy, to all acute [conditions], it has neither stem nor hole, and is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is placed upon the limb only; and this is its form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.
