Suppositories are only administered in limbs where one cannot apply cupping glasses due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places devoid of flesh, such as the breast or nose, and other similar places; and the quality of the user is that when you find suppositories that are sharp, clean, sweet-smelling without a foul odor, then take them; and put them for a night in sweet water, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then bleed from the vein and apply a cupping glass, then rub the limb so much that it becomes red, and place the suppositories on top of it; and when they are full and shrink, if this is a place where one can apply a cupping glass, then apply it, for this is worth much afterward. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the place of its ailment, and then with a sharp edge, very well, and then apply pressure; and if the veins are too close to the body after the operation, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top, until the vein is numbed; and if the veins are multiplied, put ground vitriol or alum, and similar things, on top until it is numbed. Or you put half of peeled beans on the place, and leave them until they burn at the place, this will stop it now; and if you need more, take other beans. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the bristles do not want to take hold, rub the place with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the bristle comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn; and when you see that they fall off, sprinkle powder on a piece of aloe and silk ground up, or ashes, and they will come off now. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures 
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations. 
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the follies which are described in this chapter have never been seen in any of the ancient books, nor read by letter; and for this reason the science is strange in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing except through the science of the ancient books, where I studied so much that I learned it, and by experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have shortened it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments which are administered, as I have done in these two previous chapters. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore it is necessary that we say or prologue of this book the summaries of speech and the chapters where wise men put their understanding, and dwell upon the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others. 
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is fitting that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if nothing else hinders him, such as weakness of the body, or infancy, or old age; or if his temperament is very bad, or too cold; and forbid cold foods, that is to say, cold drinks, and meat of birds and goats, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, or spreading matter in the limb; if the patient returns to his first regimen which he used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with foods that promote thick nourishment, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in broth, rice, and peas, and cow's stomach, eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things. 
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at half-brokenness it is recovered more quickly than the fracture. 
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot be properly set or soldered according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor can those which are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but do not worry, set the broken bone with a large splint which grasps and joins the limb together, as firmly as it was before; and do not remove it from its work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish it with large meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are various in many ways. 
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures. 
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others that are sharp, as the point of a pen for writing. 
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture at any small crack. 
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each condition has its own engine and its own instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings to its place; and the fracture of a bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted and clearly visible upon touch, and it gives way under pressure from the hand; and when there is neither twisting nor pain on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but there may be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It does not behoove you to move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that come later, and then extract it now subtly. 
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that for a fracture that goes into the limb, and the two parts are separated, it is now necessary to set them straight equally, just as abscesses come if they are hot; and if hot abscesses come, leave it for a few days until the abscess is calmed; then set it straight, so that you can move it lightly and wisely.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into two pieces, whether it is the hand or foot, or if it is a small limb, or two cords, or one cord and in the hand; and set the limb according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the broken limb are loosened, reset by all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and be careful that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not set correctly; if it sets beautifully, do not constrain it too much, nor press as those who bring forth by their work a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set, chastise the patient well so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other manner; and guard well that the limb be so secure that it feels no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except perhaps a little, and it is necessary to put him in a position where he feels no pain; and see to it that it is set straight, so that crookedness does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form. 
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar ones; so it is fitting to wrap them in soft and subtle linen cloths; and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg; so it is fitting to wrap them with a wide and strong bandage, for wide bandages embrace the whole large limb and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no strain; then tie around some light wadding, three turns or four according to the limb, and restrain your hand a little at all of the bandage, then go above the fracture and restrain it less, so that the fracture then moves away a little; and soften the bandage a little, as much as you take a large part of the healthy place, then take up the other bandage, and turn around again on top of the broken place; then return to the lower part of the fracture, and restrain it moderately, not too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first line above; then put between the bandages wadding of linen or cloths, so that they are all equal, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something soothing and hot to the abscess, which removes the swelling, and leave it like that for several days; then strain with your splints, and they should be half the width of a cane, cut wisely, or made from wood used for making wedges, or palm leaves, and they should be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others; and be as long as is suitable for the limb in size or largeness; then remove it on the splints as you did at first, then tie a thread above it, just as in the first time on the fracture; tighter underneath, looser above; and it is necessary that the threads are medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and be of soft flax; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen from the works of fools who make their bandages of twisted linen thread, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is not right that there be less than two finger-widths of space between each splint. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is bruised by the head of the bones after cauterizing them in their health, put under them pads of linen, or wool fleece, so that they do not bleed. 
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the heart is broken, I will say the cure hereafter. 
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not right to set all broken limbs on the first day. 
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not right to put strong splints before 5 or 7 days, or more according to your surety of a hot abscess appearing; and see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: and it is that you take flour which sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of plaster restoring fractures in many positions, and likewise for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of poultice restoring the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barleycorns and ladani and enula and asefetida and gum arabic and mugwort, each ten grains; myrrh and aloes, each five grains; alkanet nine grains; and make a powder, and mix them with the white of an egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, then use this poultice, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is worth more than many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster for twisting: take mugwort and vismalve, each X grains; myrrh and aloes, each IX grains; acacia VI grains; Armenian bole X grains, and grind well, and mix with vinegar or the white of an egg, and administer it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, and soothes the pain arising, and it uses the size of the bone, and the breakage: take new wool, and moisten it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore anything, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and properly removes pains. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and leaves of common poppy, and grind together, and make plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of plaster to restore a broken bone and to soften the remnant of an abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marsh mallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of wheat, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix it with coriander water moist, or with water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of plastering, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes during the restoration of a limb. 
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of marsh mallow, and seed of flax, bugloss, melilot, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all an equal part; and grind, and confect with water of salt, or soft water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb for restoration except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else besides, and he says it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard. 
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one must place upon the broken limb, for restoration, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense, and similar things, as we have said. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make a plaster that is good for wounds and pain: take mugwort and horsehair cut short, or bird feathers, and mallow, and bind them equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then he loosens it a little after, and takes care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that the bone has moved from its place; if not, he does not loosen it for several days. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess boils and reddens and hurts and swells, it is better to remove all the pus, and then you need plaster and bandages, and if it starts again as you did at first equally. 
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, do not untie it until after III days or IIII or V or VII; and never leave it for XX days, according to what one sees, so that the fracture heals, and the adjustment of the flesh approaches; then restrain it more than at first, and thicken its meat, as I have said before; and if you see the place dry more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there; apply therefore a poultice of lukewarm water, every time you untie it, and do this every three days, and leave a poultice on the wound for an hour; by this work you will therefore cut off the nourishment to the limb, and quickly amend what foolish surgeons do who leave the limb crooked: this is bad, and these are dangerous operations, and I see nothing else but leaving it and working it straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the diverse ways of fracture 
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck bone breaks all the bone until the syfac which is below the bone, as a hatchet or axe does; and for this reason this manner of fracture is called “haichure”. 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword strikes the bone above without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or a crack or chips of stone, or chairs on stone, or other similar things. 
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture that extends close to the membrane that is under the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is either large or small. 
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound is healed to the bone as thin as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture “capillary”; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and makes the piece of bone enter inwards, and the edges are close together like the cauldronsmiths when they strike on the cauldrons; if the stone enters inside. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have soft or wet bones, such as the skull of a child; and it occurs in all these ways of breaking where small pieces are separated, such as splinters; and I will speak about them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the traction upon them, and the inquisition at attempts, and by the corrupted flesh that is upon them. 
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	Similar hair is known by this, that when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs carefully upon it, if it appears black broken. 
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be mindful of the patient's conditions, and if you see any bad sign, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, tension, fainting, fever, and the eyes coming out forcefully and reddening, and other similar things in various states, it cannot heal without doubt. 
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeless situation, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment. 
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the disease first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the time that you can. 
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone becomes corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned occur. 
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches as far as the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the divided part thus: and that you take hold of the head of the patient firmly, and expose it on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more often than you can, and if discharge of blood comes to uncover the bone, or an abscess arises, help him with what is necessary, and fill the place with cloths softened in rose oil; and make the wound rest until the abscess that has arisen is appeased, and are sure of the discharge of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method if you cut a narrow incision in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I make another incision larger than the first. 
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of different sized incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of hardened iron; and work lightly so that you do not crush the head. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce it around, so that you administer cuts with trephines, without making sure that they do not penetrate beyond the bone on which they are used; and it must have on its point a margin or a circle that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that each one comes in its place according to the shape of the bone, so that you have trephines for all of them; and this is the form of the three ways of trephines: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put the awl on the bone and turn it back and forth until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the awl elsewhere a bit after, and do this all around, then cut with the incision tool the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pincers; and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the spinal cord. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and cut it, it is fitting that you leave the instrument which has remained on the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it is fitting that it be thinner and more subtle than the other incisor; and if there remains anything of small bones or scales, remove them lightly with the other instruments; then treat the wound with tents and dressings as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is as the Galliens say, which is safer; and praise it very highly, and this is their word. 
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to be moving; so that when you have uncovered that part, you put below the head of this lens-shaped instrument: 
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and leave the part sharp on two sides, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then strike with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly chop around the bone, and be very careful of the cloth beneath; if it is close to the bone, gently lift the bone, for one can lift it well without harm, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not extend to the skin, and the bone is cut only on top, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to scrape away that roughness and remove the scales with a fine razor which you should have in various sizes, so as to administer the most suitable one, according to the work and the shape of the fracture. 
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If kings before great razors, and afterward of more subtle ones, and do not cease to do so until it is well. 
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other types of hair-cutting and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer care according to its direction; and this is a matter not answered by him who has put his study into this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the fistula is uncovered, it behoves you to take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and place it upon the wound; then take another cloth doubled into two or three, and wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it upon the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you do not burden the fistula, then administer another bandage over it, and do not bind it too tightly only as much as to hold the wound; and leave it thus for one or two days, until the abscesses have quieted, then unbind it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and put it upon the wound, and administer now worldly medicines without biting; and see that the wound is now clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow any pus to collect, for when pus collects upon the cloth over the brain, it will corrupt and fester, and will cause the patient great harm; for when one puts something biting upon the fistula, it irritates it above. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt. 
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackening does not come except for the medicine that has been put on it, which has a particular virtue, then it is necessary that you take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and in glue one cloth, and you put it on the syphilis; then you cure it in the manner that is appropriate, until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two parts of the nose above are sometimes broken, or one by itself, for they are bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break unless it is forced to bend or twist, and then it heals. 
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you put your little finger or a small hole in the bone, and place the broken part inside your index finger, and into the pouch by force, until the bone returns according to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the knee and the bone cannot return to its place, then you must put it even with the head of a nail as thick as a thumb. 
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, do it again in the same way and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses that have formed are appeased, then apply at the head of the wound two strips of linen cloths.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you put it on one side and the other side is broken; and if the tents are so large that they fill the openings of the nose. 
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer should moisten the bandages with butter, and change them every day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened in a preparation of egg yolk and mill powder; then leave the splint on as long as the bone is strong and the cartilage hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes put goose feathers in place of bandages, and if it is wrapped with a linen cloth, and the fracture is held together, and the patient blows upon it; do what you see. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess bursts while you are working on it, put cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a drop of diascordium. 
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not come, then apply a plaster made with rue flour and powdered incense, mixed with egg yolk; then put it on light cloths and do not tie it with a bandage; and if the fracture of the bone is small and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with instruments suitable for this, and sew the incision, and treat it with things that help heal flesh and solder, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound in the bone, then treat it with splints and put canes of lead until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone 
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is completely dislocated below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only below, and is not broken in two, but merely pushed inward, so the practitioner can easily recognize it. 
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, put your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture inside, and with the other hand, set it straight. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two parts, then you must administer extension in two portions, so that it is equal. 
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth, or fracture, bind them with thread of gold or silver or silk; then apply cerate to the broken mandible and put a double cloth on it; and put on the cloth a large well-made star, or a piece of leather equal in length and width according to the mandible, and tie it up as tight as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.  
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, if it loosens on the third day, and then puts back what has changed; and put a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with plenty of egg or flour of sesame, after you have removed the scab; and put light linen over the plaster, and if the plasters dry out and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a boil comes, do as we have said many times. 
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of bone is removed; if it is very subtle, remove it with suitable instruments for this. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with flame according to your need. 
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there are none left, if the wound is wide, apply on it plasters suitable for that purpose, to generate flesh, until it is healed. 
de la forcele	from the strong hand
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong hand breaks many times forward, toward the shoulder, and the fracture is according to III manners: or it is broken and detached in two, and there are fragments, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is this: when the break is without a wound, you should have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the bone is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then set the break evenly according to your judgement, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor protrusion. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, put a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and make it thick according to your need; stretch and lift the force, and pull the sphere with your hand so that you align the fracture as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus out backwards, because it comes in straight, then it is necessary for the patient to lie often on his back, and put under the shoulder a half pillow, and push the ministers' shoulder down, until the bone of the humerus is raised. 
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then set the fracture according to your will, and if you find it broken, it is necessary that you cleave upon it; and treat the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join for any pressure, take a hold of one of the incisors that you have; but place underneath the forceceps this instrument, to guard the syfac: 
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not sharpened, and is as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two heads, as you see, and one is broad, and the other narrow, as is the break in the wound that you have made when you have treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cauterize the wound, and if the break is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, dress the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come, moisten a cloth in rose oil and alum and wine, and put it on. 
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without incision, is that you put on the bone the plaster of powder from the mill and yolk of egg, and put light bandages on top, and put a splint under the armpit if you need it; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, and then put two cloths on top of the bandages and the plaster; then take a subtle stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage up the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the sick armpit; and loosen it from each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture properly, and you see clearly that the stick does not move on the broken bone, then leave it alone for a day, and when the bandages loosen, then tighten them; and let the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the armpit to lift the shoulder up high; this will lighten the fracture by lifting the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents happen, for twenty days; then start the plaster again if you see he needs it, and remove it and leave him like that until he is restored; and it is restored at most in twenty-eight days, and less in some men. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the fracture of the shoulder 
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It sometimes happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates, and it is not possible to put it back in place except by touch; if you arrange it according to the shape of the break and reset it according to its natural form in all the ways that you can; then put powder from a mill with plenty of egg white on it, and light bandages, and put a double cloth over it.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and not below the heart, then push it up, and splint it, and do what we have said about breaking the forcele to soothe the abscess with heat. 
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot 
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in two, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it descends below, and the patient feels great pain, and shortness of breath, and all at once, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the hair on the broken bone, and everyone feels it well. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on their back, and they put a cushion between the shoulders, then they press the shoulders, and they assemble the ribs of the two sides with their hands, and subtly they make it equal in all the ways that they can, so much that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then they put on plasters and bandages above the fine plaster of salt, or other light herbs, and they wrap it in a cloth, and they tie it above the broken bone so that it does not move; and they turn the bandage roundly to the back, and they loosen it gradually, and they watch each hour the ligature, and if it loosens, they loosen it; and if it is necessary to untie it because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten yourself, and untie it, and remove the plaster, and treat what has come there in ways of cures; then they reapply the plaster, and they loosen it as much as it is healed. 
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs 
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs only comes from behind, after the back and especially in the upper part, and they do not break except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well by inquiry with two fingers. 
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And restoration is such that you put the fracture equal, as it should be. 
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a plaster, and remove it with a spatula, if you need to. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is inward, then the patient feels great pain and pressure, as well as pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lining; and the flesh has points, and all together vomits a great quantity of blood, and it is dangerous, and the ancients have described it in great detail. 
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer meats that inflate the belly, to drive out the fracture. 
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, so that warm abscesses do not come, if they have not already come. 
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, so be it healthy. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say none of us puts cupping glasses on the spot, to suck out pus, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass may draw superfluities to the spot due to the weakness of disposition. 
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the area with linen soaked in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to equalize the pressure around it, then it is cured by a pleural cure, meat, and medicine. 
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot suffer because of the bone pointing through the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to protect the vessels; and then one should trench the bone, and draw it gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and cure it with plasters until it is healed.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put it on cloths moistened in rose oil and apply it to the area; and cure it as is needed for the abscess, and let it lie often on its side or wherever it should be until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck 
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a bone breaks at the neck, and it also happens that it rains; and so too in the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know whether they will be healed or not, if you are careful and see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in several positions, and if he moves them and feels well when they are removed and nothing else, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if care is given to him. 
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it is healthy or not, see if his feet are softened, and if the accidents are in his hands, and on the back there is windiness and expulsion without will; and when he is turned onto his stomach, there is expulsion without will. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if you do not labor in its treatment. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this incident does not happen to him, it is a lighter matter. 
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you warm it if there is a hot abscess, then put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it is calmed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where he feels pain, as long as he is healed. 
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cover it on the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment made with charred material, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," put your left hand under it, and make it equal to the other hand with your power, then put plaster and a splint on it, if you need them; then remove it, and if there are any broken bones, do the same thing, and remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the breaking of the bone of the hip 
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It sometimes happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does happen, there would only be a slight reduction in height at the head; and making it long, and sloping to the side, and causing the patient pain in the area, and numbness, and swelling where it is broken. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above it, as long as you are above the fracture; and know which is the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then set that fracture equally, as long as it is in its natural shape. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it slopes inwards, have the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture appears to you. 
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it back in place, apply a plaster, then place a splint of wood or horn on top, and hold the fracture still so that it does not move; and bind the area below the ribs, as long as the joint is aligned. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if boils come, do not touch them until the boils are appeased, and put on what we have said before; then return to restoration, and extract it as it is necessary, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder 
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, so you must restore it according to one of two ways: one of which is that you take a splint of medium thickness, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two bones with two bandages and lift them up, and make the patient sit on a seat; then have someone put their broken arm on a stick until it reaches the armpit, and they should bend the stick, and then lean it against something heavy where the minister extends it downwards; then the doctor places the fracture equal to his hands together, so that the fracture returns as it should. 
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one lays the patient on his back, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two assistants that one holds what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below at all the ligament, and each stretches in his part. 
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, extract the ligature below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to their respective parts. 
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is fitting that you put one bandage below the armpit and the other towards the elbow, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the elbow, it is fitting to put a bandage lightly, without effort, as long as the fracture is equal on the place and on the elbow; then set the fracture equally as it should be, and remove it, if no abscess comes. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess should come, do not drain it until seven days have passed, and place upon it linen moistened in water and rose oil, until the abscess has subsided; then drain it, and the manner of draining it is as follows: you put a plaster on the rupture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder joint, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; and place a cloth, and drain above the shoulder joint, and above the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, unless anything prevents it, or if the bone has not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, use splints and place on the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two finger widths of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers on each side; then strain upon the splints as I said at the beginning of this chapter upon the fracture, harder and less in moving it away. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the bones, and the constriction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, leave it tied until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the tie every three days, so that itching does not swell or come to the place, where the nourishments cannot come to the member because it is too tight. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the flesh, as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these accidents occur, do not loosen the bandage for three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back with his hands on his stomach; and place a cushion full of wool evenly under the shoulder, and watch every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move or become softened by the bandages. If it straightens by the power of medicine, give him the meat we have mentioned before in part, so the meat is thin at first; and when he begins to recover, make it larger. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be held together for forty days altogether; and then one must untie them and administer baths and ointments to straighten the place. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and tight, it will remain untied for I day or II months. 
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm 
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "fosciles", one of which is small, and this is the one that enters the pouch; and the other is large, and this is the one that is below, towards the little finger; by chance the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and by chance both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken altogether. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is a small bone that is broken alone, then it must be gently stretched, and set equal.
