Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the larger muscle, it is necessary to restrain it more strongly; and extend it on a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the smaller toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed upon himself, and the cushion in front of him higher up so that the patient does not suffer any hardship; then extend the minister's arm below his hand, or at the bandage, and another minister above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the sights equal, according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place; and if there is any detached that grasps the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision on the bone, as we have said before. 
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a singular chapter; so take the cure. 
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration there arises boils, then make a dressing of cerate made of rose oil and white wax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the dressing on top delicately, until the boils are appeased. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerate, and put on a plaster of powdered mill with plenty of egg, then put on the splints, and let the splint from the fracture be now stronger, and a bit wider than the others; and know that it must have six splints or arms in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and draw tighter above the fracture than elsewhere, and always looser as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths which are on the fracture be soft and damp, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is drawn be flax, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the ligament after a few days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you water the limb with hot water, until the itching is relieved; and let the limb not be tightly restrained. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin the stretching, and if the ligaments are softened and the bone detached, and similar things, so the address. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you fear that the nourishment cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a bit and leave it like that for several days until the nourishment comes back and then extract it. 
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, then do not unbind him for 20 days. 
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Where one has a sprain or fracture, and can hold his hands to his neck, and keep his necks equal, and guard against movement and shaking, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in 30 days or 35, and by chance in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand 
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as we have two times there are small breaks, and it does not come but rather weeping many times. 
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it behoves that the patient sits straight, and be directly in front of him equally; then put his hand on the stretched cloth, and stretch the minister bones broken, and place them equal to the mirrors, as long as they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be wrapped in a linen towel. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the part of the leg below the belly of the foot, make a sphere out of cloths and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken foot; then strain with a long cloth, and let the star of heart be as large as the palm of the hand, and strain it, as it is right. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is below, it is necessary that you put a splint above, and another below on the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie the whole hand around, and tightly bind the ligature between the two. 
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of our fingers, if it is the thumb, set it straight as it should be; and take it out with the palm, and if you see that it sets a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not move; and if the fracture is in other fingers, as in the index finger or one of the others, set it straight, and tie it with the healthy finger which is next; or tie them all together, holding them tight, or put on a splint, like a pouch; and take care during restoration and placement of hot abscesses, and help those who come to you, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh 
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one ties a bandage above the break, and another below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his linen evenly to his portion; and this is when the fracture is between the bones. 
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, let one of the ligatures be towards the hip, and the other ligatures below the fracture. 
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then let the bandage be below the knee, and the extension downward; then put the hands on the bone evenly with both hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, so that no abscesses come. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down then return to your work and treatment; the ligature is done in this way. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the fracture with bandages doubled two or three times, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heels reach the root of the thigh, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the leg below the knee, and bring the head of the thread above; then turn the bandage on the leg and thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then apply eight cloths of soft rags between the leg and thigh to make the constriction equal, then begin to bind with three or four turns on the fracture; and when you go higher above the fracture, tighten less; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you have passed between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the head of the thread, as far as you reach the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this until no abscess or swelling or other similar thing comes.  
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, so that it loosens and straightens what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that grab, then it is necessary to pull them out if one can; and if one cannot, then it is necessary to split the place and extract with force; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the thigh broken when one puts splints on it, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in this restoration thus made does not ring the patient. 
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 1 day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions. 
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the path of the knee 
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that on the road of the knee there is often no breaking, but it bends many times. 
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is only a crack or a hole, and occurs with all wounds, and without wound, then it is well felt. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts what is crooked back in its place as much as it can be assembled and moved; then put on plaster, and I put a round splint if you need it, and restrain it as it should be, then observe all the arrangements that we have said for other fractures, such as abscess cautery and other similar things; apply to each accident what is suitable for it until it is healed. 
de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg 
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" and the other is called "foscile"; and there are all kinds of breaks as in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as that of the arm, equally so, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, turn them back. 
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain and it is seen clearly; and it turns below. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and set it straight, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is bad, and there are several pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; and the alignment according to your skill. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two bandages of wood shavings that can bind the leg on one side and the other, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap it twice with two bandages above and below, and tie it in the middle too, so that at this binding the leg cannot lean to the right or left, and so it is well. And no one shall administer any bandages longer than the leg, and if they are of wood, put them on the leg to prevent movement, and properly do this on the fracture where there is a wound; and move the leg every day, to see if there is a hot abscess or another accident; cure it until it is healed. 
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of bones of the foot 
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and become dislocated, and there are many other situations. 
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that a bone in the foot is broken, and you see these bones rising upon each other, so put the sick person's foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, and then now put your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, then press it so much that they return to their place; then put the plaster and bandages on top, and put under the belly of the foot a small board with two inches thick, then straighten the foot gradually, after you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things as needed. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated. 
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, if you restore them as we have said for the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and it should be one finger wider, then put beneath the foot that table which I have mentioned, and bind it tightly; and if there are two or three, or more, bones broken, put on each bone a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the table underneath the foot; and let it be placed upon the head of the table under the belly of the foot so that it holds it well. 
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have said; and treat each accident as it is appropriate. 
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone where the knife 
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, if you make her sit enlarged, then incline her to the part of her back, and have her held from behind; then fill the cavity of the woman's nature with cotton, and put in as much as your fist; then unbend the woman, and lift the back little by little, and then the cotton will jump out, as far as it comes to the entrance of the nature, and the bone will return with the fist; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days or so: the fracture will be restored, and if you see that it is not healed, take a bladder of a calf, tie a cane to the opening, and push the whole bladder into the nature; then blow into the cane until the bladder is inflated inside: the nature will return the bone to its place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man's arm or a woman's is broken, if you restore it as we have said in the bone of the hip; and these near fractures are not hidden from one who puts his study and his use to it, and understands my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For fracture, it signifies to him in several dispositions the right way of restoration: understand then. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap bandages around it and leave it for three days or until healed quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound 
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that he be cleansed now, so that the cleansings which we have mentioned testify to this. 
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, and there remains vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture in the same hour or day, so that no abscess comes. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess should come, leave the restoration until a new day, as long as the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you would bring about evil accidents. 
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the chest exposed, it is fitting that you put it straight lightly with your hands, to slight extension. 
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not seem suitable to you for setting equally with your hands, then have this instrument which is of iron, which has VII or VIII in length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this it is necessary that he imprint III or IV, according to what he may need in each cure of a fracture; and let it be round and a thick knob, so that it does not bend at compression on the limb in your work, and let it be sharp in front and thick from the middle forward, like this: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," for which it is necessary that the curved head be placed on top of the bone that appears; and the end at one time, until it returns, and is made equal to each other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instruments cannot properly grasp the bone, it is necessary that you cut off the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have power. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then use the edge of a suitable instrument for this, either an incisor or a saw, at your power; then cut what remains in the bone with sharpness and small incisions. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is put back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you have set it back in its place, then moisten the bandage with black stiptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; and do not put any cerate or anything else on the wound where there is oil, lest it should cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and bind the covering all around according to the quantity of the wound, and be very careful that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many a foolish barber has done this and caused death or corrosion on the patient, sometimes; and let the strapping be softer and more frequent than for other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, it is not right to put splints on it; but wrap around it, instead of splints, hard cloths, and bind them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the bandage on the wound has become loose, then remove what you have put on top of it all, and put a healing ointment on it, such as tetrafarmacon ointment and similar ones. 
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound. 
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is fitting that the limb be straightened out in such a way that the bone can slide down easily. 
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day they trespass, and he cannot solder but returns there again crookedly, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which it is necessary that you widen the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose pieces which cause that pain. 
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter before. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and the fracture appears on the limb, such as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not pull it at all, for death often follows, but leave it until it has decayed; perhaps it will fall away by itself after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the burns which come from the solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the shape of the limb; and by chance, it cannot make the limbs do their natural work. 
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Be careful then if the swelling is fresh: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with egg white or with oil; and put them on the swelling in compresses, and bind it well, and do not untie it for several days; and then remove it, and begin another, until the swelling is removed; or you can bind it to a well-made piece of lead, for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut above it, and make the superfluity appear; or you can shave it with a razor until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb which is weak after healing 
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and remains afterward the limbs weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tight, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not come to the limb; or from a multitude of disturbances; or from movements that are too great, or not done at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body tender, until his blood is multiplied within him; and administer a bath, and give him joy and rest; then put pitch on the limb, so that the pitch draws to great inflammation, and often bathe it in hot water, until the inflammation subsides in the limb; and returns to its natural shape. 
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the twisted limb after healing 
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb all over again, and many foolish ones have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and great evils come from it, and by chance death; nevertheless, if the dislocations and the torture are recent, it is fitting that they be softened with hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a mollifying plaster, such as good diachylon, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or you take fat figs, and crush them with bran, and similar medicines that reduce swelling. 
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation removed by continual and prolonged rubbing with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour. 
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with an iron, then you must cut to the bone, delicately with a fine knife; and put care and attention into the treatment. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations 
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury. 
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs to anyone, if it is necessary now to bring it back without delay. 
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limb swells, and by chance if one puts it back in place, it will be painful; for this reason, one should not move it while it is swollen: often it brings spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make a poultice for the patient, then leave it until the abscesses are healed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as it comes into its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of the dislocations from the head down to the feet. 
des mandibules	of the jaws 
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It sometimes happens that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are a little loosened from their places, and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down toward the ground, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and enfolds his tongue with speech. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself with several adjustments. 
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it quickly and do not delay; and in such a way that the assistants hold the head of the patient, and put their thumbs into the pocket of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be free, to even it out; and command the patient to soften them, his jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he looks at the bone to make it equal, as long as it returns to its place. 
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, even if both jaws are held together, apply hot water and oil, so that they soften slightly; do not hesitate in resetting it as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back equally, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening it, then put soft cloths on it in a cerate made of rose oil and wax, and bind it lightly with soft bands; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his arms should be placed between two cushions so that he does not move them to the right or left, nor does he exert himself to chew, but takes light food as long as the pains are gone, and the jaws are joined; and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not bother to open his mouth for eating and drinking, as long as the jaw is well joined and healed.  
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be put back into place within an hour, and are not returned to their positions, then fever and habitual soddenness will come, and by chance loosening of the bowels, and by chance vomiting of pure bile. 
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is lost; and many times they die within nine days. 
de la forcelle	from the fork 
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate from within the side of the leg and the foot, and it is dislocated sometimes at the outside, and one feels this well. 
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back and extends his arms; then press the place with your palm and it will return; then put a plaster on it and bandage it, and restrain it; and the head which is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate; if it does, and if it dislocates sometimes, then reset it in its place, as we have said; then put a plaster on it and bandage it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus the same way the head of the shoulder is reset when it is dislocated from its place.  
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one of which is that it dislocates at the part of the axle below; and the second is at the part of the buttock; and by chance it dislocates at the part above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and many times it dislocates below towards the axle, especially for those who have little flesh, for in these it is quickly dislocated; for those who have enough flesh, it is hardly dislocated, and returns with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it sometimes happens that some men have a concussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of it. 
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore it is necessary that you test it until you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment. 
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And dislocation is known when it is towards the armpit, and put difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them manifest diversity; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the armpit at the touch the head of the shoulder, just as if it were a bone; and the patient cannot bring back his hand to its nest, nor move by any movements; and also, if it is dislocated above, unless it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not difficult to reset, when it is new, or when the child is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the practitioner lifts the patient's hand high, then puts their fingers below the armpit and lifts the joint forcefully upward to its place; then the practitioner lifts the hand and extends it upward, then puts it down; it will come quickly. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in the next few days, then it is fitting that the patient be bathed in hot water; and they be given a soothing and softening lotion, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and it be administered; then the patient be laid on their back, and a wool pad of equal thickness be placed under the shoulder blade, neither too soft nor too hard, then the patient place their heel on the pad, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister hold the head of the patient so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will come back immediately now, and if you see that the resetting is according to this manner: then it is fitting that you have a man present who is larger than the patient; and be straight towards the side, and push the shoulder under the shoulder blade of the patient, and lift the shoulder blade upwards, so that the patient hangs on the arm; and another minister pulls the hand of the patient downwards towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, they can hold something heavy with them, and the dislocation will return now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting is also done in another way: and it's this, one puts a long coal in the ground, whose head be as round as a pestle, and not too big nor too small; then it is put under the patient, but that he have several cloths above it, and the patient lies along the length of the wood; then his hand is extended downwards on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take a coal of two arms in length and four thumbs wide, which has a round head to be able to enter perfectly under the shoulder blade, according to this form:  
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie upon the head of a log two cloths underneath so that he is not bruised, and place it beneath the armpit of the patient; and extend his arm along the length of the log, and tie the shoulder to the log, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on the rung of a ladder wide enough, and let the hand be extended downwards and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return in place now. 
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter how, it befits you to put under the shoulder a sphere of wool equal, then put plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and yolk of egg, upon all the shoulder and around, then bind it under the shoulder securely, and turn the bandage upon the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it befits that he rest a little, as long as the limb is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then rest more afterward five days or seven, and move it; and if it is firm and it is not softened, it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has been forced out of place by moisture or some other cause, it is necessary that you apply cautery to three holes, as it is set forth in the chapter on cauteries. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm upward, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation that is near the shoulder blade and breasts or back is made by a push and stretching of the arms, and it is administered in another place; and heals as long as it is healthy. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness in the limb, and slowness of movement, then let the patient bathe many times, until that stiffness is relieved and it returns to its original nature. 
de la dislocation dou coute	Of dislocation one must cut 
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and at points it returns; and if it is dislocated on all sides, both in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reset, for one can see it well and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick knife with the healthy one, if you can see it openly. 
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is lifted, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it as soon as abscesses may come, for if abscesses were to come, it would be a nuisance to reset them; and by chance it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is in the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by chance death may come. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that when it can be brought back, you extend their hand with your two hands; and their arms should be spread, and the hands turned according to the cut, up and down; and push the joint at its sides together, or at the root of their palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and presses from the root of the palm or where the bone is dislocated. 
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply strong extension; and let the one who applies extend the arm, and hold it so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm in every direction; once you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when he looks at the joint, put oil on the joint with his hand to soften it; then push the joint firmly until it returns to its place; and when it is in its place, apply dry plaster with egg yolk, and bind it firmly, and hang the arm at the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, untie the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not well-bound, start again with the plaster and the bandage and leave it like that for several days, until it is firmly set; then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or you put on the joint a greasy sheep's wool, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and let him go into a bath; and when he sweats, if he rubs the joint temperately, then puts the wool on again, and then goes into a bath; and thus do two or three times until he is healed; and if you see that, put on cow dung moistened and warmed with butter, and strain it on; it will return to its position. 
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand 
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is light, more than the other joints. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is done so that you put the sick hand on a table and extend the ministers' hand, and look at it evenly, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it as far as it will return to its place altogether. Then it is necessary for you to see if it is well in place; then put the sick person's back of their hand on a table, for extension and resetting. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient put the back of their hand on the table, and the healer puts their hand on top of that appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good; but if not, apply soothing poultices to the abscesses and leave them alone so they do not start again. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot suffer it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint will remain crooked; and do not harm the patient any further than that his hand is weakened and cannot grip anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; if there is no other remedy except to extract with a cautery near the case, and perhaps nothing else will work. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then unbind it and leave it like that. 
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then apply warm water, and rub it until it is healed. 
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the wrists of the hand 
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the shoulder joint is dislocated in any direction, sometimes on the back of the palm or in the palm itself; then bend the shoulder and push the dislocation back into its place as far as it will go, then hold the head of the shoulder and pull it towards the part where it is separated; and leave it for two days, and then on that day make it equal.  And at night tie it up, as we have said, and untie it during the day, and move it around, and tie it back up at night; do this often until it becomes tight, and do the same if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand; and do so as you have done before, until it heals. And do the same, when it is dislocated in another part. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Regarding the loosening of the shoulder blade from the back 
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient. 
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the limbs jump suddenly without volition, and he cannot hold them, and often some members are softened, either both thighs or both arms or one; and many times the shins move in four parts; the one that moves at the back is called "gilbositez"; its cure is that you observe whether the gilbositez has come from childhood: if there is no cure or healing altogether. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient ways of treatment were said in many words, where there is not much profit in all; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the stiffness that comes to the breast beforehand, neither engine nor feeling; and also that which comes straight on both sides, and one cannot cure but that properly which comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be extended on his face in an equal place, and have a strain under him, so that he does not bleed; then put one ember at the head in the earth form, and the other at the feet, and tie a strap below the buttocks of the patient, and the other at the haunches, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers know the straps, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two embers; and let them be well fastened, the ember as we have said, and the minister put his palms on the spine form, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a board three arm's lengths long and place it under the armpit. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should put two firebrands at the head of the patient's bed on one side and two others towards his feet; and between each firebrand above and below a hand's breadth in length; and let there be a hole in each firebrand where the cord runs, and let the firebrands be firmly set in the ground so that they don’t move. And let there be a turning firebrand between each pair of firebrands with which the cord turns; and it should have two small firebrands of a hand's length to turn the cord. Then tie the cord that is among the axles to the turning firebrand towards the head, and the other cord toward the feet to the other turning firebrand, and let each of the attendants turn his turning firebrand at full speed; and let the master place the spine straight as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equalized, put a drying plaster with plenty of egg white on top, then bandages, and then a splint from a tablet three fingers long, which should cover the area of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the vertebra, then tie it with a bandage as we have said, and use the patient with gentle nourishment, until he is healed; and if anything comes at the end of healing, you must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint we have mentioned before; and sometimes administer a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes on the posterior vertebra of the back, and one thinks that it is a dislocation; but it is the bone which appears, for which one should not have any presumption: by chance it would bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip 
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come loose through dislocation alone, and not in the same way as other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and it is more often dislocated inward, and rarely dislocated front and back. 
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of this dislocation within is such that when you join the ailing leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the ailing knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the ailing one cannot double its knee at the fire; and there is a swelling hot abscess behind, for the head of the thigh comes there.  
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who is coming to die is that this incident is contrary to those before. 
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has it in front are these: if his leg is well according to its fulfillment; however, he does not bend his knee twice without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and he retains his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he passes on his heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has it behind are that he cannot extend his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs. 
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The resetting of this kind of dislocation is such that you consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its arrangement, there is no cure; and it is not fitting that he should have presumption. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those in whom the dislocation is fresh and there are four types of dislocation, if you hasten to turn the joint and extend it inside and out and move it to the right and left; perchance it will return and need no other treatment. 
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary that you prepare a strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with both hands, or with a bandage tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand over it in such a way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then he binds it tightly with a bandage above the thigh; and another holds the head of the bandage; and they extend upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well. 
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to treat it according to its appearance. When the dislocation is in the thigh, it is necessary that you place the patient on their healthy side, then put a bandage on the root of the thigh, and the place which is below the knee, then extend the bandage upward toward the knee, and towards the groin; then have another minister hold his arms, and embrace the large part of the sick thigh, and extend it outward in a backward direction: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong cord high above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the ill leg be extended two fists longer than the other; then let it hang from the top of a post, and let it be two arm's lengths above the ground; then command a minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient, who embraces the lower part of the thigh, for the joint will now return quickly. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is down, lay the patient as we have said for him who has sciatica, and bind the bandage properly on the injured leg, and on the foot also; then put two embers, one at the head and the other at the foot, then insert an ember between the thighs of the patient in a form; and place cloths moistened with wine around it so that he does not burn the patient, then stretch each minister towards him and let the one who looks bind the dislocation equally with his hand. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on a table and press it together as we have said in the gibbosity, and lay the patient down on his healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.
